## B. ROLE CONTRACT — DESTINATION vs ROUTE  (source: LORAMER_HANDOFF.md)
## ⛔ OPERATING DISCIPLINE — DESTINATION vs ROUTE (gate-level; read every session)
<!-- LORAMER_HANDOFF_OPERATING_DISCIPLINE_V1 -->
2026-06-23 FAILURE, named plainly: after correctly grounding in the repo, Claude converted ROUTE / sequencing decisions — its OWN job — into multiple-choice questions for Russ, and repeated it after being told to stop. Russ is NOT the coder or the plan-builder; offloading route decisions onto him is a FAILURE, not caution.

- DESTINATION vs ROUTE. Russ owns DESTINATION (what the app does/is; the governing law; genuine product forks the docs don't already answer). Claude owns ROUTE (how: sequencing, which platform/grain first, build order, whether to run a step the plan already specifies, blast-radius/safety). Claude DECIDES the route from the law + the plan, states a one-line reason, and proceeds — it NEVER asks Russ to choose the route.
- ASK RUSS ONLY FOR: (a) code/write approval — every code change, migration, deploy, before it runs; (b) a genuine product fork the governing law + the existing plan do NOT already answer. Everything else, Claude decides.
- BANNED ANTI-PATTERN: presenting an option-menu for a decision Claude should make. The ask-user-question tool is for product forks + preference elicitation, NOT for offloading sequencing Claude owns. "I don't care how, just do it right once" = Claude's cue to DECIDE and proceed, not to ask again.
- CONSULT THE PLAN BEFORE INVENTING: before proposing any "new" approach, check whether the plan ALREADY contains it (2026-06-23: a full Phase-4 breadth plan + LORAMER_COMPLETENESS_AUDIT_PLAN_V1 already existed; Claude began authoring a parallel one). If the plan has it, EXECUTE it and cite it; never freelance a duplicate.
- BLAST-RADIUS STATED, NOT ASSUMED: every proposed step names its blast radius, in order of safety — read-only investigation (always safe) → backend writer (isolated) → -next UI (preview-gated) → live-path (shared read-path / any live surface = STOP-and-confirm, never automatic). Live-path changes are allowed with graduated care. There is NO Meta review and no reviewer path — a shared-surface change STOP-and-confirms because of BLAST RADIUS (every client, every live surface), never a reviewer (the Meta App Review outcome that retired the reviewer path is owned by DECISIONS). Standing PRODUCTION obligations (not a freeze): the Meta data-deletion/deauth callback stays live (permanent Meta prod requirement), the Shopify install callback is a LIVE merchant path provisioning must not break, and Google Ads live snapshots stay quota-capped while Standard Access is pending (its live status owned by DECISIONS/QUEUE). A step touching a live/shared surface states "live-path" on its face and STOP-and-confirms.
- ONE THING AT A TIME: never stack a yes/no + a paste + a new question in one turn; when Russ answers a question, the NEXT turn does the WORK — it does not ask a follow-up question.
- OWN MISTAKES WITHOUT OFFLOADING: on error, acknowledge in one line, correct the route, and proceed — never convert recovery into more questions for Russ.

## C. GOVERNING LAW  (source: LORAMER_ESSENCE.md)
# ⛔ GOVERNING LAW — READ FIRST, OBEY ABSOLUTELY (no exceptions, no reinterpretation)
LoraMer captures EVERYTHING from EVERYWHERE and stores it FOREVER (until the customer cancels).
- EVERYTHING = every grain AND every dimension every platform exposes: account, campaign, ad_group/adset, ad, keyword, search_term, placement, device, geo, age/gender, hour/day, network, video, impression-share, all conversion/action types, product/variant, geo, and every other breakdown the API serves. If the API offers it, we capture it.
- EVERYWHERE = every connected platform: Google, Meta, Shopify, WooCommerce, GA — and any platform added later.
- FOREVER = forward capture appends daily and NOTHING is ever deleted or aged out; backfill reaches each platform's retention floor.
- FULL GRAIN, WITH HISTORY, IS THE DEFAULT. If the current code captures a thin slice (e.g. account-level only, or forward-only), that is INCOMPLETE CODE TO BE FINISHED — never a constraint to design around, and never labeled "future," "phase 4," "later," or "post-launch."
- The ONLY acceptable reason to not capture something is that the platform genuinely does not serve it (e.g. Google search terms beyond ~90d no longer exist to fetch). That is the ONLY exception. Filtering artifacts, missing params (campaign_id, time_increment), unbuilt writers, and "out of scope for this change" are NOT reasons — they are work to do.
- SEQUENCING is allowed ONLY as one-change-in-flight engineering discipline (each change reconciled, blast-radius-scoped, revert-ready). Sequencing NEVER means deferring, dropping, or relabeling any capture as out of scope. Everything is in scope, now, until Russ explicitly says otherwise.
- A fresh Claude that proposes a "persist the thin slice now, fuller grain later" plan has VIOLATED this law. Capture the full grain with history in the approved build.

## ⛔ PRE-ACTION GATE (forcing function — output this line before ANY Claude Code paste or ANY UI proposal; a skipped line is a visible violation)
`in-flight: [what's running / clear] · blast-radius: [read-only|backend-writer|-next-only|live-path] · grid: [which card, or N/A non-UI] · high-stakes claim: [none | VERIFIED/DERIVED/UNVERIFIED + what]`
(The gate field is BLAST-RADIUS. Levels, safest→widest: read-only (always safe) → backend-writer (isolated) → -next-only (preview-gated) → live-path (shared read-path / any live surface = STOP-and-confirm, never automatic). Live-path is ALLOWED with graduated care. There is NO Meta review, no reviewer path, no reviewer-driven hold — blast radius on a shared surface is about EVERY client and EVERY live surface, never a reviewer (the Meta App Review outcome that retired the reviewer path is owned by DECISIONS, not restated here). Standing PRODUCTION obligations (not a freeze, not a review): the Meta data-deletion/deauth callback must stay live (permanent Meta prod requirement), the Shopify install callback is a LIVE merchant path provisioning must not break, and Google Ads live snapshots stay quota-capped while Standard Access is pending — the 15k/day Basic cap binds route decisions; its live status lives in DECISIONS/QUEUE, never here.)
High-stakes = any claim gating a destructive/rotate/delete action, a "this is a bug" diagnosis, or a blast-radius/live-path judgment. Rationale: the rules already exist; this converts the ones most often dropped under momentum (one-in-flight, blast-radius, grid-native, claim-confidence) into required visible output so a skip is caught in the moment, not after. Root cause: 2026-07-01 session — repeated rule-breaks despite the rules being present; the failure was compliance, not coverage. Do not relitigate.

- GOVERNING LAW (above): capture EVERYTHING / EVERYWHERE / FOREVER, full grain + history. A thin slice (account-only, forward-only) is UNFINISHED CODE, never a "phase-4 / later."

No standalone data/analytics surface outside the card system — a new metric/breakdown is a card (or a card's detail view), never a floating panel. Building outside the grid is a STOP; state which card it is (or why it can't be one) before proposing any UI. Root cause: 2026-07-01 floating MoneySummary panel built outside the grid built the day prior.

The store is source-of-truth only for explicit store-truth questions; each platform's value stands on its own for platform questions; offline-uploaded sales enable a valid ROAS even without online purchase. Lora holds all sources at once, distinguishes them, and explains WHY they differ (web-researching the explanation when it helps). Every metric, every surface.

A number from an unverified instrument is not a finding — it is a guess wearing a lab coat. This law would have prevented every correction of 2026-07-14/15.

- [LAW] LORA SEES EVERYTHING (Russ, verbatim, non-negotiable): Lora must SEE, KNOW, UNDERSTAND, and SAY what everything is. There is NO acceptable situation where Lora "can't see" a user's own data. Anything else claiming Lora "can't see it" IS A BUG. Every honesty failure of 2026-07-14/15 was Lora denied HER OWN USER'S OWN DATA by our code or our prompt — never a boundary.
- [LAW] THE MODEL IS ALMOST NEVER THE PROBLEM. Seven diagnoses in 2026-07-14/15 blamed the model; the code was at fault every time. Before writing "Lora inferred / hallucinated / ignored / confabulated," READ THE CODE THAT BUILT HER CONTEXT. The seven, so they are never re-inherited: (1) "regex scorer said 74.1%" — the SCORER was lying (false-failed D1, false-PASSED B5/C1); replaced by an LLM-judge validated over banked answers (117×3 passes, zero flips). (2) "C1 is a real fail / B6 predates the floor" — FICTIONAL RUBRICS never verified against metrics_daily; C1 was real (verified), B6 was fiction (Google's account-range backfill NEVER RAN, so 2020-01-27 is where OUR capture starts). (3) "B2's prompt over-reached / prompt-only fails B=3/8" — VOID: harness ran NEXTAUTH_URL=:3000 while the server was :3111, so /api/chat's internal fetch threw and buildClaudeContext was NEVER CALLED; no rule reached her. (4) "D2: she overrode the captured number" — FALSE: OBJECTIVE_RULES told her verbatim "Traffic — do NOT expect or evaluate conversions"; she OBEYED our prompt. (5) "readiness RPC renders CONNECTED as NOT_CONNECTED" — FALSE: connections fetched separately; the meter SILENTLY BLANKS (`{readiness && ...}`) on heavy clients. (6) "readiness RPC is index-mismatched (the A6 story)" — FALSIFIED by EXPLAIN: the index existed and was used for light clients; the defect was QUERY SHAPE (SELECT DISTINCT is O(client-rows); PG15 has no skip-scan). (7) "A6's timeout was the 8s ceiling / cron isn't 8s-bound" — both FALSE (A6 = missing partial index; cron IS 8s-bound). PATTERN: Claude wrote [PROVEN] on things it had DERIVED; Russ's insistence on verification caught all seven, not the resume protocol.
- [LAW] LIVE STATEMENT_TIMEOUT IS 8 SECONDS, NOT 120. supabaseAdmin → PostgREST connects as `authenticator` (statement_timeout=8s); role GUCs do NOT re-apply on SET ROLE, so 8s persists through service_role. The 120s cluster default is visible ONLY to MCP/superuser sessions — EXPLAIN ANALYZE in MCP measures against a limit real users NEVER get; any query benchmarked only via MCP is UNVERIFIED for production. Raising the ceiling is NOT the fix: every timeout found this session read millions of rows to return dozens; written correctly they run 30–72ms. The 8s limit is a SMOKE ALARM, and it protects the pooler — a slow query holds a connection, and a handful stall the whole app.
- [LAW] THERE IS NO STAGING DATABASE. An RPC/migration can only be proven where it is applied. CREATE OR REPLACE is the revert path. State this before every migration.
- [DESTINATION — RUSS, LAW TIER] **FOUNDATION FIRST.** INFRASTRUCTURE, DATA, and LORA are the indispensable three; they guide all future expansion. Everything else is built on them or waits. QUALITY GOVERNS THE CLOCK — delay is ACCEPTED where quality requires it; a date never licenses shipping a foundation we know is wrong. This is a DESTINATION (Russ owns it), not a route: it does not tell Claude what to build next, it tells Claude what may never be traded away to move faster. ⛔ RUSS DID NOT NAME A NEW LAUNCH DATE when he stated this. DO NOT RECORD ONE. The standing launch date is the LAST one Russ stated in his own words — its value lives in DECISIONS (LORAMER_SOFT_LAUNCH_JULY22_V1), never restated here — with delay accepted if quality requires it, and per the CLAIM-CONFIDENCE law, accepting a delay is a risk accepted, NOT a date change. (2026-07-15 precedent: a wrap banked "launch moved off" from Russ merely tolerating a delay; he never said it, and Russ caught it, not Claude.)
- [LAW] WEB-FIRST DIAGNOSIS (LORAMER_WEB_FIRST_DIAGNOSIS_V1, 2026-07-19; SCOPE WIDENED 2026-07-23) — BEFORE proposing or authoring ANY build, fix, detector, schema change, OR diagnosis — NOT only a platform / API / tool error — SEARCH THE WEB for (a) the KNOWN CAUSE of that exact error and (b) an EXISTING PUBLISHED FIX or implementation. Vendor docs, SDK issue trackers, community repos, MCP servers, Stack Overflow. If a usable base exists, ADAPT IT rather than authoring from scratch. THE ADAPTATION IS NOT A SHORTCUT PAST VERIFICATION: found code is read IN FULL and Gate-A-proven exactly like code we wrote — never trusted on sight, never pasted on reputation. Found code is a STARTING POINT, never an answer. WHY: 2026-07-19, the Meta code-1/subcode-99 fix was fully engineered — split the call, batch by id, split-on-failure — and only THEN searched; the search confirmed 1/99 is a DOCUMENTED payload-size 500 whose standard remedy is exactly ID-batching, and surfaced meta-ads-mcp already carrying Meta creative error-handling to adapt from. The engineering was right, and it was still the expensive way to get there: hours of live probing to re-derive a published answer, with no cross-check against how anyone else solved it. Searching first is not a substitute for thinking — it is what stops us paying twice for the same knowledge. SCOPE WIDENING, 2026-07-23 — why "error" was too narrow: T0#4 (the account-row-per-day detector) was a clean BUILD with no error to diagnose, so the LETTER of "a solution to an error" never fired while the SPIRIT plainly did — nothing was searched (history / web / repo) before the detector was engineered. The trigger is now ANY build / fix / detector / schema change / diagnosis. THE ENFORCER is the VISIBLE THREE-FIELD HEADER on every such paste — HISTORY · WEB · REPO ([[SEARCH-BEFORE-NEW]] for history; this law for web; CHECK-FIRST for repo) — spelled out in LORAMER_HANDOFF's WEB-FIRST REPORT REQUIREMENT: a paste without it is MALFORMED and rejected on sight, before its content is read. HONEST LIMIT (stated, never implied away): the header's PRESENCE is inspectable — a paste either shows the three fields or it doesn't; whether a search TRULY preceded and informed the code is NOT inspectable by any guard (no check sees the temporal order of a search vs authorship). The header makes skipping VISIBLE; it cannot make searching HAPPEN — that stays discipline.
- [LAW] FIX-WITH-GUARD — A FIX IS NOT DONE UNTIL A MECHANICAL CHECK FAILS WHEN IT REGRESSES. The guard ships in the SAME commit as the fix; a fix without its guard is not shipped. PROSE IN A DOC IS NOT A GUARD. A guard must be SEEN TO FAIL against the pre-fix code — a guard never observed failing is not a guard, it is a comment. Build it on the CODE (the thing that cannot lie about itself), never on a doc (a doc can be honest-but-false). Guard the CLASS, not today's instance: if the next writer/page/field can reintroduce the bug and the check still passes, it guards nothing. Where a pattern lives in N files, do not guard the convention — COLLAPSE IT TO ONE SOURCE and guard that (the settleRevenue / META_BREADTH_FORWARD shape): we fix files, we do not enforce rules. PROOF THIS IS NEEDED, 2026-07-15, both from this repo: (1) ESSENCE has said capture EVERYTHING/EVERYWHERE/FOREVER since day one, and 10 Meta breadth dimensions froze at their ship dates anyway, with two cursors sealing backfill_complete=13/13 over a permanent hole — nothing failed, the cron returned 200, and ~1,900 rows/client/day silently stopped existing. The law was written, present, and read every session; it changed nothing because nothing MECHANICAL enforced it. (2) The 2026-06-20 client-context fix was real, correct, and shipped — and regressed three weeks later at team/page.tsx:22 because the pattern lived in six files and no check could see the seventh. A law you cannot fail is a wish. If a mechanical guard is genuinely not achievable for a rule, SAY SO plainly rather than shipping a check that manufactures false confidence — an unenforceable guard is worse than none: it reads green exactly like sync_state read backfill_complete=13/13 while forward capture did not exist.

## ⛔ DETERMINISM OF JUDGMENT [LAW]
Given the same question over the same finite data, Lora must reach the same conclusion 100% of the time. Her answer may change ONLY when new or different information exists — and when it does, she must be able to say WHY it changed (attribution, not silent drift). This holds across model upgrades: Opus 4.8 → 4.9 → any successor must not change a conclusion.
MECHANISM (the model is never the thing that decides):
- NUMBERS: computed in code via ONE canonical settle. Lora REPORTS, never derives. (Fix #1 Part B is the first brick.)
- RECOMMENDATIONS: derived from deterministic, versioned, testable RULES. The model's job is to EXPLAIN the rule's output in English, never to originate the judgment.
- PROSE: not bitwise stable and does not need to be. If literal repeatability is ever required: hash (question + data fingerprint + memory state + prompt version + corpus version + model ID) → return the cached answer.
- MEMORY is INSIDE the exception: a stored correction IS new information. Requirement is ATTRIBUTION — Lora must cite which correction changed her answer.
- MODEL UPGRADES are gated by the eval. No model reaches users until the golden set passes with CONCLUSIONS unchanged. Precedent: Sonnet→Opus flipped B1 and D2 with identical code; the eval caught both.

[VERIFIED 2026-07-14, Anthropic docs — platform.claude.com/docs/en/about-claude/models/model-ids-and-versions + /overview]
- claude-opus-4-8 is a PINNED SNAPSHOT, not an alias. From the 4.6 generation on, the dateless ID IS the snapshot; Anthropic does not update weights or config under an existing ID. New versions ship under new IDs. LoraMer is correctly pinned.
- CAVEAT: weights are fixed per ID, but SERVING INFRASTRUCTURE (request router, safety classifiers, sampling logic) can change under the same ID. So bitwise output stability is NOT guaranteed even on a pinned ID. This is why determinism must live in code, not in the model.
- CAVEAT: every model ID has its own deprecation/retirement schedule. Migration is eventually mandatory; the eval gate is what makes it safe.
- CAVEAT: Opus 4.8 uses adaptive thinking with effort defaulting to HIGH on all surfaces — a live variance source today.

## ⛔ GROUNDED RECOMMENDATIONS / THE CORPUS [LAW]
- Lora's recommendations are grounded in a FROZEN, VERSIONED best-practice corpus — NEVER a live web search. Live search is a determinism bomb: same data, different day, different answer, no new information from the user. A corpus VERSION BUMP is new information: dated, attributable, eval-gated, roll-back-able.
- The corpus feeds the RULES, not the prose. Every recommendation CITES its source (corpus / the user's own correction / the platform's own doc). "Argue with her" is the product: she shows her sources, the user can dispute them. Same moat as multi-source metric provenance — explaining WHY, applied to judgment.
- POSITIONING (true, defensible): Google's and Meta's recommendation engines are structurally conflicted — their revenue IS the advertiser's spend. LoraMer's revenue is a subscription. Frame as INCENTIVE ASYMMETRY, never "they lie" — some of their advice is good, and overclaiming hands a skeptic an easy win.
- HONESTY BOUND: much of marketing canon is contested (brand vs. performance, attribution, incrementality). Never claim Lora knows THE truth. The claim is that she shows her sources and can be argued with.
- RISK FLAGGED, UNRESOLVED: ingesting third-party copyrighted marketing material into a corpus whose output is resold is real IP exposure, distinct from a human reading it. Public-domain / licensed / primary sources / Russ's own writing are clean. NOT legal advice — needs a real lawyer before the corpus scales.

## ⛔ "MAKE LORA YOUR OWN" — WHAT THE PROMISE CAN AND CANNOT CASH [LAW]
CAN: her name/voice/tone; the org's definitions (net sales, value model, ROAS basis); their documents; their retained corrections; their guardrails. All config, all real.
CANNOT: "a different mind" (weights are shared and rented); "she knows everything about us" (the librarian SELECTS — omission is the mechanism, not a bug); "exclusively yours" (direct tension with the cross-agency LoraMer tier — a POSITIONING FORK, unresolved: exclusive-yours vs compounding-across-agencies cannot both be headlined); "you own her" (implies portability/export — a moat hole if yes, marketing if no; decide knowingly).
COST LAW: per-org memory grows the briefing packet forever → input tokens rise per turn, per customer, permanently. Cost scales with ENGAGEMENT; best customers cost most. Must be budgeted before memory ships.
COPY GUARD: "she learns YOUR WAY OF WORKING" is true and defensible. "She BECOMES yours" is the check that bounces.

## HOMEPAGE / BOTTOM-OF-PAGE MESSAGE (banked for the two-door homepage item)
"The model is rented. The memory isn't." Every tool in the category runs on the same frontier AI anyone can rent — that's the starting line, not an edge. LoraMer's edge is what it KEEPS: every platform captured at full grain from the day you connect. So when Shopify and GA disagree, Lora shows BOTH, labeled by source, and explains why — the question every other tool hides from. A competitor can rent the same model tomorrow. They can't rent your history.
GUARDS: (a) "from the day you connect" is load-bearing — backfill is bounded by platform retention; never let it be edited into "all your history." (b) The cross-agency brain is ANONYMIZED PATTERNS, not data — any line implying Lora learns across agencies must read that way, or it reads as "your client data feeds your competitor."

If a change makes Lora more confident but not more provable, it is wrong.

## D. OPERATING RULES  (source: LORAMER_DECISIONS.md — OPERATING PROTOCOL + STANDING PRINCIPLES)
- SESSION START GATE is the ONE authoritative resume protocol: ESSENCE → CONTINUE_HERE + REQUIRED READING (in full) → HANDOFF + ROADMAP → state NEXT STEP → wait for "go". Act only on what's read THIS session; repo is sole source of truth; panel+memory lag. | HANDOFF:1-31 | do not relitigate.
- REPORT FORMAT (2026-06-09): every report ONCE, IN FULL, in ONE fenced code block; commands/verbatim inside via <<<START>>>/<<<END>>>; OUT.txt retired; no file delivery. | HANDOFF:27, CONTINUE_HERE | do not relitigate.
- END-OF-DAY TERSENESS (2026-07-10, Russ): after giving Russ the code/paste for the NEXT action, STOP — no "what's next" preview, no holding-open / next-steps lists, no postamble; he gets it in the next exchange anyway (redundant). Half the words in general; keep momentum. SHARPENS the standing terse-delivery rule (HANDOFF:189/276 — no recaps, no "here's what I'm going to do," just the step) with the post-paste angle — not a new independent rule. (Build-parity corollary already banked, do NOT duplicate: HANDOFF:374 — never name a machine in a build command; `npm run build` runs on EITHER.) | LORAMER_EOD_TERSENESS, 2026-07-10 | do not relitigate.
- 7/14 LAUNCH POSTURE (LORAMER_LAUNCH_POSTURE_V1, 2026-07-10, Russ): the launch MISSION = complete the legacy→-next port + RETIRE legacy by 2026-07-14. Move with DELIBERATE SPEED — fast, but RIGHT > FAST holds: no half-fixes, no do-it-twice, no backtracking; get it right the first time. Sharpens EVERYTHING-LAUNCH-CRITICAL (:17) + RIGHT>FAST (:16) with the concrete mission. | LORAMER_LAUNCH_POSTURE_V1, 2026-07-10 | do not relitigate.

Deliver RESULT + DECISION + PASTE; elaborate ONLY when asked; half the words. Sharpens the standing terse-delivery rules (HANDOFF:189/276) + END-OF-DAY TERSENESS (LORAMER_EOD_TERSENESS above). | LORAMER_LAUNCH_POSTURE_V1, 2026-07-10 | do not relitigate.

A thing Russ trips over at 11pm is not automatically launch-critical. OUTPUT: ONE ranked list, each item with its blast radius and an honest size. THEN Russ decides whether the date holds — the date decision comes AFTER the list, not before. ⛔ DO NOT BUILD ANYTHING BEFORE THIS LIST EXISTS.

## G. SETTLED-DECISIONS INDEX — do-not-relitigate, the complete map  (source: LORAMER_DECISIONS.md)

- BEDROCK — TOTAL DATA CAPTURE: on connecting ANY source, auto-capture+backfill every grain/dimension/metric to the deepest the platform allows + forward daily. ENFORCEMENT: (1) auto-backfill on connect, (2) forward covers ALL grains, (3) completeness gate gates "onboarded", (4) fetched-but-unpersisted = DEFECT. No session may narrow this. | LORAMER_HANDOFF.md:35-43 | do not relitigate.
- AUTO-BACKFILL-ON-CONNECT design: on connect → cursor 'pending' (never run inline); cron sweep drains lap-by-lap; 20-lap safety cap; honors per-day self-reconcile HALT; never oscillate into a wall (L51); managed=full speed, Woo=extra-gentle. | CONTINUE_HERE (queued 2026-06-18), ROADMAP Data-Completeness-Onboarding | do not relitigate (design settled; build pending).
- RIGHT > FAST, always. Senior-engineer (20+yr) rigor. NO same mistake twice. | HANDOFF Operator-Level-Truth | do not relitigate.
- EVERYTHING IS LAUNCH-CRITICAL by default for July 14, 2026 — only exceptions: named next-phase (design then write) or external constraint (Meta/Google review). | HANDOFF GOSPEL, ESSENCE | do not relitigate.
- DESKTOP=MOBILE PARITY — ONE responsive app, verify both per increment, never fork. | HANDOFF GOSPEL + STANDING | do not relitigate.
PARITY — CANONICAL DEFINITION (2026-07-08, Russ): the BARE word "parity" ALWAYS means MACHINE PARITY — the iMac and the MacBook Air can perform ALL the same tasks, fully. A machine that cannot complete a build/push/deploy gate the other can is a MACHINE-PARITY VIOLATION to fix, not a footnote to route around. All OTHER parities MUST carry an explicit qualifier and are never written as bare "parity": "desktop=mobile visual coherence" (one responsive app, both surfaces coherent, never forked — cf. :18); "-next↔live capability parity" (the cutover flip gate — a FLIP surface is at parity when it shows the same data, correctly, as the current app; cf. LORAMER_NEXT_FLIP_PROGRAM.md); "connection-state probe parity" (all 5 platforms probed equivalently); and misc technical axes (quota parity, forward/backfill parity, writer-behavior parity) which stay locally qualified at their use site. Rule: if a doc says "parity" with no qualifier, it means MACHINE parity; every non-machine sense REQUIRES its qualifier. | LORAMER_PARITY_GLOSSARY, 2026-07-08 | do not relitigate.
- The MOAT is the intelligence/memory/recommendations layer, NOT the dashboard. Goal = real-world recommendations & growth, not data display. | HANDOFF North-Star, ROADMAP Strategy | do not relitigate.
SEARCH-BEFORE-FORKING (2026-07-08, Russ): Before presenting ANY principle, default, product direction, or governing rule as if it needs deciding — i.e. before offering Russ a fork/option-menu on something that sounds like product law — Claude MUST first search past chats (conversation_search) and the repo docs for a prior decision. If it's already decided, CITE it and build to it; do NOT re-offer it as open. The tell that triggers this: Claude catching itself about to say "your call / here are the options" on anything resembling a settled principle. Re-litigating closed decisions is the single biggest waste of Russ's time. This session alone, mobile-first-standard, store-truth ROAS law, and "both ROAS labeled" were all already banked and got mistakenly re-opened. Searching first turns "let me propose this" into "you already decided this, building to it." | LORAMER_SEARCH_BEFORE_FORKING, 2026-07-08 | do not relitigate.
TWO-SOURCE VERIFY (2026-07-09, Russ): the relitigate/settled gate requires BOTH stores — the repo docs AND past chats (conversation_search). A single-store check is NOT "verified": searching the repo alone and finding nothing does NOT license "this is new/unsettled" (and vice-versa) — a decision can live in either store, so a one-store miss produces false "this is new" conclusions, the exact way settled calls get re-opened. Repo-only = still UNVERIFIED. Applies to SEARCH-BEFORE-NEW and SEARCH-BEFORE-FORKING alike: check both, or the gate did not pass. | LORAMER_TWO_SOURCE_VERIFY, 2026-07-09 | do not relitigate.
CONTRADICTION STOP (2026-07-09, Russ): when an instruction contradicts a banked GOVERNING LAW / ESSENCE / settled DECISION, Claude Code HALTS — it does NOT execute it, does NOT silently comply, and does NOT quietly "improve" it into compliance. It flags the contradiction in ONE line WITH the citation (which banked rule, and where), states the conflict plainly, and waits. The banked law wins over an in-the-moment instruction UNLESS Russ explicitly overrides it AS an override (knowingly changing the law) — not by accident. Executing a law-contradicting instruction is a failure even when the instruction came from Russ; the correct move is halt-flag-cite-wait, then let Russ confirm-as-override or restate. | LORAMER_CONTRADICTION_STOP, 2026-07-09 | do not relitigate.
PROOF-TARGET DEFAULT (2026-07-18, Russ): when a probe or Gate-A needs a client with REAL data, DEFAULT to FoamOh — clientId 957d484e-d0c4-4dd0-b382-d8499d556252 · Meta act_916558565662035 · Google Ads customer 7688521852 · GA4 properties/302128252 · Shopify dreamboard1.myshopify.com — window 2024, ESPECIALLY Nov–Dec 2024 (Black Friday peak, FoamOh's richest conversion history; recent windows read empty — it has ~$0 current Meta delivery). VERIFY FoamOh actually returns the SPECIFIC dimension being probed in that window BEFORE trusting it; fall back to a fleet sweep ONLY if genuinely absent, and SAY SO. Proof-target ONLY — changes NOTHING about capture (every client still gets everything, always). | LORAMER_PROOF_TARGET_FOAMOH_V1, 2026-07-18 | do not relitigate.
FIRST-CLASS DIMENSION DEFAULT (2026-07-18, Russ): anything Lora might PIVOT on gets its OWN breakdown_type (first-class, queryable via query_breakdown), NEVER folded into extra JSON — UNLESS a real reason (genuine unusable row-explosion, or it is not a queryable axis). Applies to EVERY fill going forward (the G-FILL/M-FILL/S-FILL/W-FILL/GA-FILL queue). extra JSONB is for NON-pivot attributes (ids, secondary labels, ratios), never for a dimension a user would slice by. (Supersedes the M-FILL#2 probe's field-widen-into-extra recommendation → attribution windows ship as a first-class breakdown_type.) | LORAMER_FIRST_CLASS_DIMENSION_DEFAULT_V1, 2026-07-18 | do not relitigate.
HISTORY-FIRST (2026-07-18, Russ): before ANY build / probe / spec on a topic, FIRST search the full chat history on that EXACT topic (conversation_search) + the repo docs, SYNTHESIZE what was already decided / built / attempted / rejected, and FOLD that synthesis INTO the Claude Code instruction itself — so no flight ever re-derives or re-litigates settled work. This makes the anti-relitigation discipline MANDATORY and UP-FRONT, not occasional-and-reactive: the synthesis is a required PRECONDITION of the instruction, the same forcing-function role the completion-gate plays for capture. Operationalizes DO-NOT-RELITIGATE and sits alongside SEARCH-BEFORE-FORKING (:21) + TWO-SOURCE VERIFY (:22) — those say "don't re-open a settled fork"; HISTORY-FIRST says "front-load the whole prior record before you even scope." | LORAMER_HISTORY_FIRST_V1, 2026-07-18 | do not relitigate.
DONE-MEANS-COMPLETE (2026-07-18, Russ): "done" for any capture family = COMPLETE against the AUDIT's vendor surface (docs/LORAMER_DATA_COMPLETENESS.md — every grain/dimension/metric the platform genuinely serves), NOT "a writer exists." This is ENFORCED IN CODE by the capture-completeness gate (scripts/check-capture-completeness.mjs, run in `npm run guard` = the pre-push gate): it FAILS the push when a `captured` family is a slice of the vendor surface or is captured-but-unwired from breakdown-registry.ts. THE GATE WINS: docs mirror the gate; if a doc says "done" and the gate disagrees, the gate is right. Work the fill queue IN ORDER; no new un-audited work jumps ahead of an open fill. Operationalizes BEDROCK/TOTAL-DATA-CAPTURE (:14) with a machine enforcer — a green writer is not done, a green gate is. | LORAMER_DONE_MEANS_COMPLETE_V1, 2026-07-18 | do not relitigate.
REPORT-TRANSFER DEFECT (2026-07-18, tracked infra issue — NOT repo-fixable): the Claude Code → chat report transfer TRUNCATES long / box-drawing / symbol-heavy payloads to BLANK. Regression began ~2026-07-18; the same reports transferred fine for ~3 months prior → it is an infra/harness-level regression, likely needs a Claude Code update / an Anthropic bug report, and CANNOT be fixed in this repo. INTERIM PROTOCOL (a tourniquet, not the fix): reports print SHORT — a one-line verdict + only the load-bearing evidence lines, in PLAIN ASCII (no box-drawing, no │═ , no emoji); the full detail is written to a file (e.g. /tmp/<task>.txt) that Russ opens directly. When the transfer is fixed, retire the tourniquet. | LORAMER_REPORT_TRANSFER_DEFECT_V1, 2026-07-18 | do not relitigate (until the infra fix lands).
LORA-COMPLETENESS AUDIT — NEXT MAJOR ARC (2026-07-18, Russ): after the capture fill queue, the next arc is the LORA-COMPLETENESS audit — the mirror of the capture-completeness audit, one layer up: does Lora actually USE everything captured? Six layers — (1) queryable, (2) retrieved, (3) in-context, (4) interpreted, (5) cross-referenced, (6) remembered. - CLAIM-CONFIDENCE RULE (binds chat-Claude every session AND Lora in-product; obey, do NOT narrate): Before stating any factual claim, rule, or generalization, internally classify it — VERIFIED (read this session: docs/code/DB, or just searched — state plainly, cite source only when it adds something), DERIVED (reasoned from something verified — show the reasoning step, not a label; if the derivation can't be shown it's a guess, not derived), or UNVERIFIED (memory / pattern-match / clean-sounding generalization not checked — do NOT state as fact; either verify first via search/read/probe, or say "I haven't verified this — want me to check?" and stop). Banned move: stating an unverified claim in a confident, verified-sounding voice. A tidy authoritative-sounding generalization is the HIGHEST-risk case — treat the urge to state a clean rule as the trigger to verify, not to assert. Do NOT label sentences as ceremony; the classification is an internal gate on whether/how to speak. Surface uncertainty ONLY when a claim is actually unverified. Test every claim: could I show where this came from right now? If no → check it or flag it, never assert. | Root cause: 2026-06-24 session, repeated confident-but-unverified assertions (e.g. "breadth has no purge clock", "I can't see your settings") each corrected only by Russ pushing back — the exact failure this rule exists to stop. | do not relitigate.
- CLAIM-CONFIDENCE — HARD VERIFY GATE: Any factual claim, rule, or generalization that a build, commit, deploy, or recommendation depends on, and that is not VERIFIED this session (read/searched), MUST be verified through Claude Code BEFORE proposing action — not "want me to check?", check first. Never build, commit, or recommend from memory, pattern, or a prior-session summary. Unverified + load-bearing = stop and verify, every time. (Non-load-bearing asides may still be flagged as unverified.) | 2026-07-03 (strengthens the claim-confidence rule above; supersedes the "want me to check?" wording for load-bearing claims) | do not relitigate.

- [LAW-ADJACENT, VERIFIED 2026-07-15 — the invariant the fix rests on] An ACCOUNT-GRAIN ROW IS WRITTEN ON EVERY DAY ANY GRAIN IS WRITTEN. Proven, not assumed: platform domain first confirmed COMPLETE via pg_stats (n_distinct=5, exactly {google,meta,ga,shopify,woocommerce} — no sixth value can hide from the test); then max(date) all-grain IS NOT DISTINCT FROM max(date) account-canonical for 23/23 clients with data, and the sharper per-client×platform test (28×5) returned the EMPTY SET — zero divergences anywhere. This invariant is EMPIRICAL, **NOT schema-enforced**. | LORAMER_LATEST_DATE_ACCOUNT_GRAIN_V1, 2026-07-15 | do not relitigate.
- [ACCEPTED RISK 2026-07-15 — MARKED, not hidden] LOUD-NULL → QUIET-STALE. Pre-fix, a heavy client's latest-date failed LOUD (null — obviously broken). Post-fix, IF a writer ever emits breakdown rows for a day without the account row, it fails QUIET: a stale date that looks real. That is a strictly worse failure MODE, accepted deliberately because the null is failing for 100% of heavy clients TODAY and the invariant holds fleet-wide. The trade is only sound while the invariant holds — hence the QUEUE item to enforce-or-guard it (constraint, or a coverage check flagging any (client,platform,date) with breakdown rows and no account row). If that item is dropped, this risk is unmonitored. | LORAMER_LATEST_DATE_ACCOUNT_GRAIN_V1, 2026-07-15 | do not relitigate.
- [VERIFIED 2026-07-15 — SET-identity, not merely MAX-identity] The 3 EXTRA sites narrow a row SET, so max-equivalence was NOT sufficient and was proven separately. money/latestMoneyDate + store-detect/latestStoreDate: their old predicate was account + breakdown_type='' with NO breakdown_value; rows at account grain with breakdown_type='' AND breakdown_value<>'' across 28 clients × 5 platforms = **EXACTLY 0**, so the added filter excludes NOTHING that exists → set-identical (money's 90-row window + its extra.money scan are byte-identical too). ga-overview had NO breakdown_type filter at all, so it DID include account rows of other breakdown_types; its value is unchanged by SQUEEZE — old_set lies between new_set and all-grains, and max(all-grains)=max(account-canonical) was proven for every client×platform. hasGaEver cannot flip either: the same test showed every client×platform with ANY rows also has account-canonical rows (pf_acct_max was never null where pf_max was non-null). | LORAMER_LATEST_DATE_ACCOUNT_GRAIN_V1, 2026-07-15 | do not relitigate.
- [FINDING 2026-07-15 — do not misread this as index-only] money/latestMoneyDate selects `date, extra`. `extra` is NOT in the 035 INCLUDE list (which is platform, spend, revenue), so this site gets an **Index Scan with heap fetches** (up to 90 rows), NOT an Index Only Scan. Expected and fine — it still uses the partial index and is a large improvement — but it is the ONE site of the six that is not index-only. Recorded so a later reader does not assume index-only across all six and mis-cost a change. | LORAMER_LATEST_DATE_ACCOUNT_GRAIN_V1, 2026-07-15 | do not relitigate.
- [LESSON 2026-07-15 — why the original audit undercounted 3→6] A PARTIAL grain filter is an INDEX MISS THAT LOOKS CORRECT. The 8s audit grepped for latest-date queries with NO grain filter and found 3; it missed ga-overview (entity_level only), money and store-detect (missing breakdown_value) because they LOOK filtered. A partial index is all-or-nothing: the planner must prove the query implies the FULL predicate (all three columns) or the index is silently unusable. When auditing partial-index coverage, grep for the sites that DON'T match the predicate EXACTLY — not for the ones with no filter at all. | LORAMER_LATEST_DATE_ACCOUNT_GRAIN_V1, 2026-07-15 | do not relitigate.

- [VERIFIED 2026-07-16 — CORRECTS THE "UNSEAL" FRAMING, which was MINE and WRONG] Filling a Meta breadth hole needs NO cursor write. The 6 writers touch sync_state ZERO times (grep), and the 6 thin routes touch it zero times in CODE — their only "reference" is the header comment stating the fact (api/backfill/meta-device/route.ts:4: "STATELESS bounded-range loop … NO cursor / NO sync_state (the drain's rangeLap owns the 'meta_device' cursor)"). backfill_complete=13/13 gates EXACTLY ONE line — drain-registry.ts:155 `if (st?.backfill_complete) return { done: true }` — i.e. the DRAIN's rangeLap ONLY. It does not gate the thin-route path at all. So a hole fill = invoke the existing routes with explicit startDate/endDate. Do NOT write cursors "for consistency": a cursor write would be a lie about what the drain did, and the drain's cursor is correct — it DID reach floor. | LORAMER_META_BREADTH_HOLE_FILL, 2026-07-16 | do not relitigate.
- [LESSON 2026-07-16, RUSS'S FRAMING — banked at HIS instruction because the error was his and the refutation was code] **(a) THE CURSOR "UNSEAL" NEVER EXISTED.** The G1(b) spec called for a sync_state cursor write to "unseal" meta_device/meta_video (backfill_complete=13/13) before the hole could be filled. It was asserted for hours, carried forward from a prior-session summary, and it was FALSE: the 6 writers touch sync_state ZERO times and the 6 thin routes touch it zero times in CODE — they are STATELESS and take explicit startDate/endDate (api/backfill/meta-device/route.ts:4 says so in its own header). backfill_complete gates EXACTLY ONE line — drain-registry.ts:155, the DRAIN's rangeLap — and nothing on the fill path. The fill needed no cursor write and no new code; it was 78 invocations of routes that already existed. **(b) 33.2s/client/DAY DOES NOT EXTRAPOLATE.** The spec predicted 17 days × 33.2s ≈ 564s/client, "far past the 680s budget", and specced a cron/paging plan around it. MEASURED: the whole 16-day hole cost **98s/client** — because the writers use monthChunks(), so a 16-day range is ONE chunk costing the same CALL COUNT as one day (time_increment=1 returns every day in one report), just more rows. ~3× one day, not 17×. The cron/paging plan was solving a problem that did not exist. **THE RULE: MEASURE, DON'T REASON — AND CHALLENGE THE FRAMING EVERY TIME, INCLUDING RUSS'S.** A spec handed down with confidence is still a hypothesis; both of these were refuted in minutes by reading code and running one dryRun. Inheriting a framing is how a prior session's guess becomes this session's fact — the exact mechanism behind G3 (a doc attesting a FETCH, read as persistence) and G1 (sync_state reading complete over a hole that had no forward writer). | LORAMER_META_BREADTH_HOLE_FILL, 2026-07-16 | do not relitigate.

- [LESSON 2026-07-16 — RUSS'S, banked at his instruction] **READ THE ARTIFACT, NOT THE SCREENSHOT.** Two hypotheses were built off a screenshot of the rejection + a visual read of the page, and both were wrong in ways the actual bytes settled in minutes: the page already said "LoraMer" 11 times, and the split spans had no whitespace. A screenshot shows what a human SAW; the artifact shows what a machine READS — and the objection came from a machine-or-reviewer reading the artifact. Same family as the parity-audit law (an INVENTORY question cannot answer a CORRECTNESS question) and as G3 (a doc attesting a FETCH, read as persistence): each is a claim about a thing, mistaken for the thing. - [DECIDED 2026-07-16] **GEO REFERENCE ACCUMULATES, NEVER MIRRORS.** Google phases IDs out (REMOVAL_PLANNED) and drops them from later CSV versions. - [DECIDED 2026-07-16] **NO METRO/DMA IN THE CSV.** Google's geotargets CSV carries no Metro/DMA target type — 100% of the metro grain is unresolvable from it (~210 US DMAs). - [DECIDED 2026-07-16] **PRESENCE vs INTEREST IS NOT A DUPLICATE.** The same criterion id carries both LOCATION_OF_PRESENCE (physically there) and AREA_OF_INTEREST (showed interest) with separate real spend — Bath Fitter US: $1,748,320.27 presence vs $38,354.24 interest. Summing them double-counts. The suffix is stored in breakdown_value at write time and is signal, not noise. Never normalize it away. | LORAMER_GEO_RESOLVER_V1, 2026-07-16 | do not relitigate.
- [DECIDED 2026-07-16] **NO breakdown_value MIGRATION.** The suffix parses off deterministically at read (split ':' then '/'). "Dead" here = holds nothing live; it is NOT a recommendation to delete. | 2026-07-16 verify | do not relitigate.
- [DECIDED 2026-07-16] **THE SWITCHER SIGNAL IS clientId, NOT THE ROUTE NAME.** TopBar receives clientId from Shell (Shell.tsx:37): null on the all-clients Shell, set on every per-client page. That is the "is there a current client?" signal — the client switcher uses it to KEEP WHERE on a per-client page vs route to the profile from the all-clients list (LORAMER_NEXT_SWITCHER_LIST_NAV_V1). Do NOT pathname-match route names — they rot. The SAME clientId signal guards the chat empty state (LORAMER_NEXT_CHAT_EMPTYSTATE_NAME_V1), because clientName is a truthy "All clients" on the portfolio Shell and clientName-truthiness would render a broken possessive ("All clients's"). | TopBar.tsx, ChatLauncher.tsx, 2026-07-16 | do not relitigate.
- [DECIDED 2026-07-16] **THE ONLY UI INSTRUMENT IS RUSS.** Bugs 1–3 (2026-07-16) were ALL found by Russ clicking on his phone, on prod, signed in as owner. No gate, test, or guard touches the UI (there is no test suite; the 28/28 eval + freshness gate never render a page). The whole-surface UI BEHAVIOR audit remains OWED and UNSCHEDULED (see QUEUE). Until it runs, every UI defect ships until a human happens to hit it — treat "it built + tsc passed" as ZERO evidence a surface behaves. | 2026-07-16 | do not relitigate.
- [DECIDED 2026-07-16] **A PUSH IS NOT A DEPLOY.** Every commit-and-deploy flight MUST confirm a deployment EXISTS and reads READY against the EXPECTED commit before any Gate-B check is handed to Russ. On 2026-07-16 every local gate read green — build PASS, tsc 0, freshness 10/10, commit on origin/main — while prod kept serving the OLD code, because Vercel silently created NO deployment for be58a07/9b14d16 (git-push deploy creation broke ~21:10Z; see QUEUE ★DEPLOY-WEBHOOK). Nothing in the pipeline noticed; Claude Code caught it only by explicitly querying list_deployments. Without that check, Flight A would have been reported shipped and a Gate-B "failure" would have sent us hunting a bug that did not exist. A green local build proves nothing about what prod is serving — verify the live deployment's commit + READY state, every flight. | 2026-07-16 | do not relitigate.
- [DECIDED 2026-07-16] **iOS FLEX MIN-WIDTH: A SCROLLER IS NOT ENOUGH.** `.md table` already carried overflow-x:auto — the scroll container was correct and in the right place the whole time. It was overruled because .bubbleAssistant, .scroll and .panel computed min-width:auto as flex items, so the table's intrinsic nowrap width propagated up the chain to .panel. .inputBar is a SIBLING of .scroll inside .panel, so a widened panel carries the send arrow off-screen with it — the arrow was never mis-placed, the panel was panned. ANY scroll container inside a flex chain needs min-width:0 on EVERY flex ancestor or it does not fire on iOS. Headless WebKit does NOT reproduce this — it honors the scroller. Fixed 2026-07-16 (LORAMER_NEXT_CHAT_FLEX_MINWIDTH_V1). | do not relitigate.
- [DECIDED 2026-07-16] **HEADLESS CANNOT SEE THE iOS FLEX BUG.** Playwright WebKit contained a 976px 10-col table at 390px BEFORE the fix — table scrolled internally, panel stayed 384, arrow at right 370, document 390 — while the bug was live on a real iPhone in BOTH Chrome and Safari at that exact moment. A headless render measurement is NOT evidence about this class of defect. Assert the CSS INVARIANT (min-width:0 present on the flex chain; overflow-x:auto on .md table and .md pre), or test on a real device. Do not build a guard whose green means nothing. | 2026-07-16 | do not relitigate.
- [DECIDED 2026-07-16] **REACT STATE LAGS INSIDE A SYNCHRONOUS CALLBACK.** react-grid-layout 1.5.3 fires onBreakpointChange THEN onLayoutChange in the SAME synchronous call stack (lib source ResponsiveReactGridLayout.onWidthChange, lines 174→175). A guard reading React STATE set by the first callback is STALE inside the second — setState batches/defers, refs do not. CardGrid's `isMobile` guard read the lagging `bp` state, so entering the sm breakpoint wrote the sm w:1 `stacked` layout into the DESKTOP layout, and autosave persisted it → the dashboard-cards-collapse-to-70px bug. FIX (LORAMER_NEXT_GRID_BP_REF_V1): read a bpRef.current set synchronously in onBreakpointChange. RULE: any guard inside a synchronous callback chain must read a REF, not state. Introduced 2026-07-09 (bfe1a3d), live one week, found 2026-07-16 by Russ noticing collapsed cards. | do not relitigate.
- [DECIDED 2026-07-16] **A CODE FIX DOES NOT HEAL WRITTEN DATA.** The sm-leak persisted w:1 desktop layouts into dashboard_layouts; fixing the leak stops NEW corruption but leaves the already-written rows (9, all one user, 2026-07-16) collapsed on every load. DETECT-AT-LOAD heals them: discard a desktop layout matching the corrupt signature (all items w:1 AND all x:0, ≥2 items) and fall back to the PAGE's own default (storeDefaultView on store pages, else defaultOverviewView) — no DB write, no migration, reversible, heals on next visit; the next autosave persists it. Chosen over a migration because only one user was affected. RULE: when shipping a fix for a bug that WRITES, always ask what is already written and heal it too. | LORAMER_NEXT_GRID_BP_REF_V1, 2026-07-16 | do not relitigate.
- [DECIDED 2026-07-16] **dvh DOES NOT SHRINK FOR THE KEYBOARD.** dvh/svh/lvh account for the browser's retractable ADDRESS BAR, NOT the on-screen keyboard. The keyboard shrinks the VISUAL viewport and leaves the LAYOUT viewport untouched, so a position:fixed sheet at 100dvh stays full-height and mis-registered against the visible area (the Ask-Lora sheet panned on keyboard dismiss). Nothing in the codebase listened to window.visualViewport — zero grep hits. BIND a fixed sheet to visualViewport (height + offsetTop) or it never knows where the screen is. The page bleeding through the gap (ClientPage's 'Change account', the ROAS rules box) was the SAME root: an opaque panel covering where it THINKS the screen is. FIX: LORAMER_NEXT_CHAT_VISUAL_VIEWPORT_V1 (visualViewport → CSS vars on .scrim, 100dvh fallback). | 2026-07-16 | do not relitigate.
- [DECIDED 2026-07-16] **A LYING COMMENT IS HOW A BUG SURVIVES.** chat.module.css:3 claimed 100dvh was used "so the keyboard shrinks the sheet." False. claude-tools.ts:118 claimed entityLevel was "Ignored for other breakdown types." Also false — metrics-query.ts:422 honors it for any type. Two false statements in code on the same day, each hiding a real defect, each found only while looking for something else. A comment that describes INTENT instead of BEHAVIOR is worse than no comment: it stops the next reader from looking. When a comment and the code disagree, the comment IS the bug report. | 2026-07-16 | do not relitigate.
- [DECIDED 2026-07-16] **A TRUE PREMISE IS NOT A DIAGNOSIS.** The visual-viewport chat fix (78de5ab) rested on two VERIFIED facts — dvh does not shrink for the keyboard, and nothing listened to visualViewport (zero grep hits). Both true. The fix DID NOT WORK (Russ confirmed on device, Chrome + Safari, unchanged). Facts that are true AND load-bearing-sounding are the most dangerous input to a build, because they survive every check except the one that matters: does the bug go away. Ship a fix ONLY when the failure has been REPRODUCED and the fix is proven against that reproduction. ★UI-OVERFLOW was never reproduced outside Russ's phone, and four theories in a row were wrong — each internally coherent, each derived from a CSS read + an engine that does not reproduce the bug. | 2026-07-16 | do not relitigate.
- [LESSON 2026-07-16] **POSTGREST 1000-ROW CAP.** Any PostgREST RPC that returns SETOF (a table / rows) is SILENTLY capped at 1000 rows AND returned UNORDERED — no error, no warning. An aggregation that can exceed 1000 groups MUST return a SINGLE jsonb array (the groups live inside one scalar row, where the row cap cannot bite). Caught in G2 2A Gate-A by a distinct-count mismatch (1000 vs 3169): a top-N over a silently-truncated, unordered set is a WRONG ANSWER THAT LOOKS RIGHT. The SETOF→jsonb return-type change needs DROP+CREATE, not CREATE OR REPLACE. | LORAMER_BREAKDOWN_SQL_AGG_V1, 2026-07-16 | do not relitigate.
- [DECISION 2026-07-16] **SQL-SIDE BREAKDOWN AGGREGATION = the scoped RPC `query_breakdown_agg`** (migration 038): a client-anchored GROUP BY on idx_metrics_daily_client_platform_bt_level_date, returning a jsonb array of (breakdown_value, parent_entity_id, sums); the JS layer keeps entity-level scope + canonicalize + sort + value-ASC tiebreak + topN + notes, so it stays byte-identical to the cent. PostgREST `db-aggregates-enabled` was REJECTED — it opens aggregate surface on EVERY table for EVERY caller to solve one query. Do NOT raise again. | LORAMER_BREAKDOWN_SQL_AGG_V1, 2026-07-16 | do not relitigate.
- [LESSON 2026-07-16] **PAYLOAD IS A GATE, NOT JUST TIME.** G2 2B measured DB execution at ~300ms (passing an 8s check) while the return-all-groups RPC handed back **32.4 MB** for ga_landing_page — 80,638 groups moved over the wire and JSON-parsed in a serverless lambda to return 20 rows. An 8s statement_timeout check ALONE would have waved this through. MEASURE THE PAYLOAD, not just execution time. Fix: a bounded topN RPC (migration 039) does ORDER BY + LIMIT in SQL → 4.5 KB. | LORAMER_BREAKDOWN_BOUNDED_TOPN_V1, 2026-07-16 | do not relitigate.
- [DECISION 2026-07-16] **BOUNDED-RPC SCOPE.** bounded = a NEW tool type (geo / ga_* / age_gender) OR an existing type at an EXPLICITLY-requested entityLevel (Google device/hour at ad_group/keyword). The 14 EXISTING tool types at their DEFAULT level keep the all-groups path, preserving byte-identical (proven, 6 pairs). The bounded branch THROWS if canonicalize is set — canonicalization collapses values AFTER aggregation, so a SQL topN taken BEFORE the collapse ranks the wrong things. Never silently degrade. | LORAMER_BREAKDOWN_BOUNDED_TOPN_V1, 2026-07-16 | do not relitigate.
- [DECISION 2026-07-16] **A GENERATED SCHEMA CHANGES WHAT A GUARD CAN PROVE.** Once claude-tools' query_breakdown enums GENERATE from breakdown-registry, "schema == registry" is tautological — a guard comparing them is always green. The drift guard was re-pointed at REGISTRY INTEGRITY (both files generate from the registry; every geo tuple is resolvable) — a real, build-blocking failure, proven RED with `next build` never running. Live-DB reachability (is every CAPTURED tuple declared?) stays the SEPARATE non-build script (scripts/breakdown-reachability-check.mjs) — CI has no network. A green build guard is not "Lora sees everything." | LORAMER_BREAKDOWN_REGISTRY_V1, 2026-07-16 | do not relitigate.
- [LAW, 2026-07-17] **THE FRESHNESS GATE PROVES THE DIGEST MATCHES ITS SOURCES. IT DOES NOT PROVE THE SOURCES AGREE WITH EACH OTHER.** On 2026-07-17 the session opened with a stale RUSS ACTION #1 telling Russ to go read a Google OAuth rejection surface for a gate closed the day before. CONTINUE_HERE:580 said OPEN. DECISIONS:443 said CLOSED. Every hash was green, 10/10, the whole time. ROOT CAUSE: the 07-16 OAuth-closure paste wrote the ledger and regenerated the digest but never updated CONTINUE_HERE, which is what §E reads from. The gate could not catch it because it is a consistency check, not a truth check. RULE: when a decision CLOSES something, update EVERY doc that asserts it is open — the ledger AND the resume path. Grep the closed thing by name across all gated source docs before the wrap. The ledger is authoritative when docs conflict, but a conflict that reaches a session opener has already cost the session. THIS IS THE THIRD TIME IN TWO DAYS: SECURITY_POSTURE 7.9 claimed the reviewer login was dead infra (wrong, and would have talked a session into deleting live Shopify compliance); claude-tools.ts:118 described entityLevel behavior the code did not have; chat.module.css:3 claimed 100dvh shrinks for the keyboard. A green check that answers a narrower question than the reader assumes is the recurring defect in this project. FOURTH INSTANCE, same day: the digest's §H open-queue index sliced the QUEUE at a "DONE — DO NOT REBUILD" marker and silently omitted EVERY item banked after 2026-07-15 — the entire G2 arc's follow-ons, ★UI-OVERFLOW, ★SUPPORT-BOT, and the rest. The items were in the QUEUE file the whole time and every hash was green. A condensed index is a CLAIM about completeness. If it cannot defend that claim, it must not be presented as the open list. Fixed 2026-07-17 (LORAMER_DIGEST_H_COMPLETENESS_V1: §H now selects OPEN items by meaning — block-grouped, terminal-status, position-independent — with only the fenced DONE appendix skipped; proven by a deliberate below-marker append that the old slice dropped and the new extractor catches). ⚠ STILL UNFIXED, SAME CLASS, NAMED NOT FIXED: §C's honesty-clause selector in build-resume-digest.mjs takes essence.split('\\n').filter(l=>l.trim()).slice(-1)[0] — the LAST non-empty line of ESSENCE by POSITION; append anything after the honesty clause and the digest silently swaps in the wrong line. (The header/fence extractors fail LOUD via must(); the slice(-1) fails SILENT, like §H did.) | LORAMER_SOURCE_CONFLICT_GATE_V1 + LORAMER_DIGEST_H_COMPLETENESS_V1, 2026-07-17 | do not relitigate.
- [LAW, 2026-07-17] **NEVER WRITE DOWN A FACT ANOTHER DOC OWNS. POINT AT THE OWNER.** 2026-07-17 recon: ~10 volatile facts were hand-copied into ~27 live places across ESSENCE, HANDOFF, SECURITY_POSTURE and CONTINUE_HERE §E. Five of the seven silent-drift defects of 07-16/17 lived in ONE class — external approval status (Meta/Shopify/OAuth/Standard-Access). The doc set is NOT overbuilt; each doc has a unique authoritative core (ESSENCE=law · DECISIONS=status/ledger · QUEUE=backlog · CONTINUE_HERE=narrative+opener · HANDOFF=manual · SECURITY_POSTURE=security · REGISTRY=dimensions · RESUME_INSTRUCTIONS=resume-wording). The COPIES are the disease. THE LESSON FROM THE REGISTRY (2026-07-16): prevention beats detection. Two files that had to agree by hand did not, and the fix was not a better checker — it was ONE declared source with the rest generated; drift became IMPOSSIBLE instead of detectable. Apply the same shape to docs: one owner per fact, everyone else POINTS. A STATUS DOC IS A FUTURE LIE WITH A TIMESTAMP — an AI will happily write one; it looks like diligence; every hand-copied status is a lie waiting for the source to move. WHAT CANNOT BE COLLAPSED: "what is next" is a JUDGMENT — the QUEUE has no priority field and ordering is explicitly Russ's call, re-decided per session; it stays AUTHORED and gets a CONTRADICTION CHECK, not generation (★SOURCE-CONFLICT-GATE must verify §E's named next-item still reads open in the QUEUE). And session NARRATIVE is irreducible authored history — a generator would omit or fabricate it, so it is written by hand and left as dated snapshots (frozen history is NOT drift; only LIVE assertions drift). WHAT SHIPPED 2026-07-17 (LORAMER_DOCS_SINGLE_OWNER_V1, the DELETION half — the board + generated-§E + the gate stay QUEUED as the post-launch completion, deliberately NOT built five days from launch): deleted/pointered ~the live copies in ESSENCE (2), HANDOFF (4 + the dead June-3 state block, ~96 lines), SECURITY_POSTURE (5), CONTINUE_HERE §E (5); corrected the stale "NEXT BUILD = G2" opener (G2 closed 07-16); retired the self-admittedly-stale INVENTORY from the gated set. | LORAMER_DOCS_SINGLE_OWNER_V1, 2026-07-17 | do not relitigate.
- [POINTER, 2026-07-17] **EXECUTABLE RULES LIVE IN CLAUDE.md, NOT HERE.** The ONE-CHANGE-IN-FLIGHT rule was banked as prose in HANDOFF/ESSENCE/DECISIONS and broken FOUR times in two days — because DECISIONS is where the STRATEGY Claude reads a rule, and reading it there cannot bind the EXECUTOR (Claude Code) who receives the mid-flight paste. Banking a repeat-offense rule as more prose is the FAILURE MODE, not the fix. It now lives as a REFUSAL gate in CLAUDE.md (LORAMER_CLAUDE_MD_INFLIGHT_GATE_V1), which the Claude Code harness auto-loads every session with no paste — the one place it can actually fire. RULE-HOME LAW: a rule broken more than once needs an ENFORCER, not another entry; it belongs in CLAUDE.md (binds Claude Code) or a build guard (binds the compiler), never in a doc that is only read. | LORAMER_CLAUDE_MD_INFLIGHT_GATE_V1, 2026-07-17 | do not relitigate.
- [LESSON, 2026-07-17] **THE ANTI-COPY GATES FOUND THEIR FIRST VICTIM IN THEIR OWN FILE.** 2026-07-17: while adding the ownership gates to CLAUDE.md, Claude Code found CLAUDE.md:37 asserting the chat model is claude-sonnet-4-6 while the code read claude-opus-4-8 (Opus floor = law, G10). A copied code-fact, drifted to the wrong value, in the file that now forbids copied facts. THIS EXACT DRIFT ALREADY COST US ONCE: on 2026-07-16 prod Lora was silently running Sonnet while the 28/28 eval measured local Opus. Same fact, same disease, different surface. THE FIX IS NOT THE VALUE. Correcting the value leaves a copy that drifts again. CODE OWNS CODE FACTS. A doc may POINT at where a value lives; it may not STATE the value. "Correct today" is what every one of the 27 copies was on the day it was written. - [DECISION, 2026-07-17] **ONE LORA, ONE MODEL.** Banked 2026-07-14 as OPUS 4.8 EVERYWHERE; the reasoning is recorded here because it was argued and settled. THE CAPABILITY FLOOR (2026-05-23): the insight banner IGNORED a client directive. Escential's profile said "Ignore ROAS as a primary performance metric for this account." Extraction worked, user_notes carried it, the code was correct — Haiku ignored it anyway, because in 50-word mode it could not follow a negative instruction while the ROAS number was the most flag-worthy thing on screen. THE MODEL WAS THE LIMIT. A banner that violates a client's declared value_model is confidently wrong on the first surface any user sees — the same failure class as the Display hour-0 midnight bid-down. value_model is law; a model that cannot honor it makes the law decorative. THE CONTINUITY LAW (Russ, 2026-07-17) — the stronger argument: Project 14 banks ONE LORA per client across all surfaces, picking up where the user left off. One mind cannot be three models. If banner output enters conversation history that chat later reads, the quality floor of the whole conversation becomes the WORST model that ever wrote into it — a shallow read poisoning a deep one, permanently, in the store. The 05-23 failure was not a banner bug; it was one mind having a bad thought and writing it down. ROUTE-BY-DIFFICULTY IS THE RIGHT ANSWER TO A QUESTION WE ARE NOT ASKING. Claude argued it on 2026-07-14 — Opus for chat, Haiku for the blurb, standard practice. It assumes surfaces are independent. Ours are not. That pushback was WRONG and is recorded as wrong. COST IS NOT THE ARGUMENT. Measured: $10.16 across every client over six weeks; heaviest user $4.10. Opus 4.8 at $5/$25 is ~1.67x Sonnet. Cost has never been the gate. Capability and continuity are. | LORAMER_ONE_LORA_ONE_MODEL_V1, 2026-07-17 | do not relitigate.
- [PATTERN, 2026-07-17] **DECISIONS GET MADE AGAINST TODAY'S IMPLEMENTATION, NOT THE ROADMAPPED DESTINATION.** The insight bar was roadmapped 2026-06-10 as an investigator that explains WHY. On 2026-07-14 Claude argued its model from the blurb it IS rather than the investigator it is SPEC'D to be, and reached the wrong answer. A roadmap item is a destination; decisions about a surface must be argued against its DESTINATION, not its current shape. Check the roadmap before deciding anything about a surface's architecture. | LORAMER_DECIDE_AGAINST_DESTINATION_V1, 2026-07-17 | do not relitigate.

- [LAW, 2026-07-17] **EVERY AUDIT SO FAR COMPARED US TO OURSELVES.** Three capture audits passed while Shopify, Woo and GA hour grain was being discarded at the writer. They asked "do we capture Shopify?" — yes — and never asked "what does Shopify's API OFFER, and what fraction do we store?" The reference was always our own inventory, registry, or writers. A writer that stores 40% of what an API serves passes every audit whose reference is that writer. SAME SHAPE AS TWO PRIOR LESSONS: the 07-11 legacy-to-next audit asked EXISTS/PARTIAL/MISSING — an inventory question that cannot catch behavioral bugs. G2 (07-16) found 118 tuples captured and unreachable — the READ side of this same disease; the WRITE side was never checked. THE ONLY AUDIT THAT ANSWERS IT enumerates what each platform's API OFFERS — from the platform's own published docs, not from our code — and diffs that against metrics_daily. Any audit whose reference is our own code cannot find what we never asked the API for. (The build queue: QUEUE ★PLATFORM-SURFACE-AUDIT; the first known hole it would surface: ★HOUR-GRAIN-CAPTURE-HOLE.) | LORAMER_PLATFORM_SURFACE_AUDIT_V1, 2026-07-17 | do not relitigate.

- [DECISION + VERIFIED 2026-07-22] **LORAMER_CONN_FAILURE_STREAK_V1 — connection-health stops SILENTLY masking a persistent failure (SLICE 1, RECORDING-ONLY, shipped).** THE DEFECT (recon 2026-07-22, verified live on Shelley woo 23c697bb): src/lib/connection-health.ts classifies any 5xx/timeout/429/406 as TRANSIENT (TRANSIENT_RE matches `\b5\d\d\b`), so recordConnectionResult's `authClass==null` branch and recordConnectionAuthFailure's `indeterminate` probe branch both returned SILENTLY — health stayed 'healthy', last_error_at null, FOREVER, even though shelleykyle.com host-500'd on every forward fire for 12 days (base frozen 07-19; cron_runs errored=1/rows=0 every fire).
