- [DECISION + VERIFIED 2026-07-23] **LORAMER_QUERY_COMPLETENESS_V1 SLICE 5 — stale_tail measures against the CAPTURABLE FRONTIER, not the raw window end (kills the nightly healthy-client false alarm; T0 #2, shipped).** DEFECT: stale_tail compared lastCaptured to the window's endDate; when the window ends TODAY, today is not yet capturable (the forward cron runs 08:00-10:59 UTC), so EVERY healthy client tripped amber during the nightly pre-window gap (~00:00-08:00 UTC = 8pm-4am ET) until the window advanced the frontier — a caption that fires on healthy clients trains the user to ignore it. (Surfaced by slice-4's Gate-A observation + the 07-23 capture investigation: the whole fleet sits at 07-21 pre-window BY DESIGN, not failure — utc_now was 04:29, before the 08:00 window; zero streaks; meta/ga fully healthy.) FIX (query-completeness.ts): `capturableFrontier(now)` = the last day the forward cron is EXPECTED to have captured — UTCtoday−1 if today's window has finished (now past FORWARD_WINDOW_END_HOUR_UTC), else UTCtoday−2. DERIVATION, STATED: the cron (/api/cron/sync) captures resolveDateWindow('YESTERDAY') (sync/route.ts:161); its window is 04:00-06:59 ET so the ET date == the UTC date → captureDate = (run's UTC day)−1 in EST and EDT alike (confirmed live: the 07-22 08:18 UTC run wrote 07-21). computeContribution clamps the stale comparison end to min(window.endDate, frontier); a past-ending window is unaffected (endDate < frontier → measures the raw end). `now` is injected (default new Date()) so it is testable and the routes pass the real clock. LAG_TOLERANCE_DAYS stays 2, now measured FROM THE FRONTIER. `FORWARD_WINDOW_END_HOUR_UTC=11` is NOT a free hardcode — the guard RE-DERIVES it from vercel.json's forward schedule (max hour + 1) and fails the build on mismatch, so the rule follows the schedule if it moves (the "read the cron config" requirement, enforced mechanically). VERIFIED: (a) guard EXTENDED — behavioral seen-to-fail at now=2026-07-23T04:29Z (pre-window): a HEALTHY client captured through the frontier (07-21) on a TODAY-ending window must NOT be stale_tail (pre-fix measured raw end 07-23 → gap 2 → stale → build fails), and a client 2 behind the frontier (07-19) MUST be; + static — the vercel.json re-derivation (independently computed hour 10+1=11, matching the constant). (b) GATE-A on REAL inputs (getCoverageForWindows + readHealthForClients vs prod; only `now` and case-c's streak injected + named) 5/5: PRE-window (04:29Z, frontier 07-21) a real healthy client (google/meta at 07-21) NOT captioned + Shelley woo (07-19) STILL captioned; POST-window (12:00Z, frontier 07-22) both still correct; Shelley + a synthetic live streak → capture_failing still WINS over stale_tail. tsc 0, guard all-green, build 0. The nightly design-note from the 07-23 investigation is now MOOT — the flag no longer fires fleet-wide nightly. | LORAMER_QUERY_COMPLETENESS_V1, 2026-07-23 | do not relitigate.
- [FINDING + VERIFIED 2026-07-23] **LORAMER_HEALTH_UI_FLAG_MUTED_LORA_V1 — a feature flag silently disabled a truth-telling surface, the SAME defect class as the masking it existed to reveal.** NEXT_PUBLIC_SHOW_CONNECTION_HEALTH_UI was UNSET in production before 2026-07-22 (found OFF during the [[LORAMER_CONN_DEGRADED_STATE_V1]] slice-2 ship, which set it ON — that entry owns the incident; this one owns the CLASS). VERIFIED mechanism (read this session, not asserted): src/app/api/intelligence/route.ts:30 gates whether `connectionHealth` is populated onto the intelligence payload on this flag, and src/lib/intelligence/build-claude-context.ts:1125-1137 renders the connection-health honesty block ONLY when that array is present — so with the flag OFF the block never reached Lora's prompt (intelligence-types.ts:664 states it outright: "absent → no honesty block in the prompt"). CONSEQUENCE: the flag gated NOT ONLY the new 'degraded' block but the PRE-EXISTING 'reconnect' warning (LORAMER_CONNECTION_HEALTH_V1) — so for as long as it was OFF, Lora could never tell a user that a connection's LOGIN had died (reconnect) OR that capture was persistently failing (degraded). A dead credential was invisible to the one surface whose job is to name it. THE CLASS: a flag that defaults a truth-telling surface OFF is the same failure as connection-health masking a persistent 500 — both leave a real, knowable problem unspoken; the flag just masks it one config layer up. Now ON in production (Production ="1", verified via `vercel env pull` 2026-07-22; Preview still unset — affects PR previews only, not the deploy target). DURABLE GUARD (NOT built, filed): a truth-telling surface (honesty block, reconnect/degraded notice, any "we can't see X" warning) must not sit behind a default-OFF flag; if flagged at all it defaults ON and the flag only SUPPRESSES for a named reason — the same "masking needs an enforcer, not a note" logic that [[LORAMER_CONN_FAILURE_STREAK_V1]] applied to the streak. | LORAMER_HEALTH_UI_FLAG_MUTED_LORA_V1, 2026-07-23 | do not relitigate.
- [DECISION + VERIFIED 2026-07-23] **LORAMER_ACCOUNT_ROW_INVARIANT_V1 — the account-row-per-day invariant is now a live-DB detector, guard-enforced (T0 #4, shipped).** THE INVARIANT (uniform, no family exemption): for every (client_id, platform, date) with ANY row in metrics_daily, a row with entity_level='account' AND breakdown_type='' AND breakdown_value='' must exist for that same (client_id, platform, date). It is the schema-UNENFORCED assumption the six latest-date reads rest on ([[LORAMER_LATEST_DATE_ACCOUNT_GRAIN_V1]]: money · store-detect · client-metrics · portfolio-metrics · ga-overview · clients/metrics); a captured day missing its account row makes those reads skip it and return a STALE (or null) "latest captured date" with NO error. DETECTOR: added as a SECOND assertion inside scripts/check-capture-landing.mjs (reuses its pg plumbing, no runtime code touched) — flags `--invariant-only [--guard] [--gate-a] [--prove-exact]`. It enumerates distinct captured days per (client,platform) via a LOOSE INDEX SCAN (recursive CTE, one index seek per date = O(distinct-days), NOT O(rows) — a naive GROUP BY/DISTINCT times out on the 4.8M-row heaviest pair; EXPLAIN ANALYZE 122 days in 243ms) and diffs against the account-grain days. RUN 2026-07-23 (read-only): 38,605 (client,platform,date) tuples checked, 733 violations — ALL Shelley Kyle (23c697bb) woocommerce, 2016-10-22..2018-12-10, 1–3 order/product rows/day and no account row; the range ENDS exactly at the 2018-12-10 host-500 deep-backfill wall ([[LORAMER_QUEUE_OF_RECORD]] #7 / the Woo Shelley re-capture stall). No other client/platform violates. GATE-A (real-input, no fixtures, no writes): excluded 3 real account dates from a clean client's comparison set → the detector flagged EXACTLY those 3 and nothing else (PASS). BASELINE AS DATA: scripts/account-row-invariant.baseline.mjs holds the ONE entry as an EXACT (client,platform,[from..to]) window — proven bounded (`--prove-exact` injects a synthetic Shelley woo 2025-06-15 OUTSIDE the range → guard exits 1), never a blanket client+platform mute. SPLIT — CODE-GATE vs DATA-GATE (DELIBERATE, do NOT re-merge): `npm run guard` stays 100% HERMETIC and sits in the Vercel deploy chain (vercel.json has no buildCommand → Vercel runs `npm run build` = `npm run guard && next build`), so a data condition can never brick a deploy. This DB-dependent check runs ONLY via `npm run check:data`, wired into the local pre-push gate (`npm run prepush` = build + check:data) and NEVER into guard/build/Vercel. It FAILS LOUD (exit 2) when SUPABASE_DB_URL is absent — a silent no-op is worse than no check; a missing URL at the pre-push gate means the environment is misconfigured and must stop the push. (An earlier revision wired it INTO guard with a skip-safe fallback for Vercel; that coupled deploys to data state, so it was moved out — the re-merge is what the flag-site + this entry forbid.) ROUTE CALL still standing: a STALE baseline entry (the data got FIXED) is a loud WARNING, not a failure — data improving must never block a push; the entry is then owed removal. The baseline CLEARS when QUEUE #7 re-captures those days. SPAWNED: COVERAGE-FLOOR-CHECK (QUEUE) — coverage.ts minMaxFor() may report Shelley's woo floor as 2018-12-11 (first account row) not 2016-10-22 (first any row), understating her history to Lora. Guard GREEN on current main (733/733 baselined, 0 NEW). | LORAMER_ACCOUNT_ROW_INVARIANT_V1, 2026-07-23 | do not relitigate.
- [DECISION 2026-07-23] **NO GIT PRE-PUSH HOOK — deliberate, not an oversight (pairs with [[LORAMER_ACCOUNT_ROW_INVARIANT_V1]]).** No husky / lefthook / simple-git-hooks and no .git/hooks pre-push was installed to auto-run `npm run check:data` (verified read-only 2026-07-23: no .husky/, .git/hooks holds only inert *.sample templates, core.hooksPath unset, no hook dep). REASON — a push-time trigger is the WRONG trigger for a data-integrity check: data can break with NO commit (a bad backfill, a cron gap, a merchant outage each corrupt metrics_daily without anyone pushing), so a hook firing only on push would miss the exact failures the check exists to catch, and would also bolt a ~13s live-DB scan onto every push. `npm run prepush` (= `npm run build && npm run check:data`) exists as a MANUAL convention; that it is manual is KNOWN, not overlooked. Until the durable answer lands (a SCHEDULE, not a hook — QUEUE ★SCHEDULED-DATA-CHECK), the executor rule in CLAUDE.md (run `npm run check:data` before any push to main + report it) carries it. | 2026-07-23 | do not relitigate.
- [DECISION 2026-07-23] **LORAMER_NEXT_META_ACCOUNT_SORT_V1 — the -next "Choose a Meta ad account" picker sorts named accounts A→Z (case-insensitive) FIRST and numeric-only-named accounts (name blank / = the id / all digits, e.g. 12909870) LAST by id ascending — TWO GROUPS ON PURPOSE; do NOT "simplify" to one localeCompare.** A single sort floats number-named accounts to the TOP (digits collate before letters) — worse than unsorted. Proven on the REAL 199-account cotebrandmarketing@ list (Gate-A: 191 named A→Z + 8 numeric-only last, id ascending). Display-order only, sorts a COPY, zero data change; ONE source = src/lib/next/sort-meta-accounts.ts (ClientPage.tsx imports it). | LORAMER_NEXT_META_ACCOUNT_SORT_V1, 2026-07-23 | do not relitigate.
- [DECISION + VERIFIED 2026-07-23] **LORAMER_LORA_TOOL_DECISION_LOG_V1 — the L2-retrieval instrument stores a FAMILY LABEL, not the question text; migration 044 APPLIED (Gate-A passed).** WHY family, not question_text: chat content already lives LINE-FOR-LINE in client_conversations (role ∈ {user,assistant} + content, one row per turn), so storing the question here would DUPLICATE it — the L2 skip-rate needs only the DECISION + the classified breakdown family. NEW table lora_tool_decisions (id · org_id · client_id · family · tool_called · tool_name · turn_index · model · created_at; indexes on created_at, (client_id,created_at), (family,created_at)); additive, NO existing constraint touched, NO FKs (the fire-and-forget logger must NEVER fail a turn). CONVERSATION REFERENCE DELIBERATELY OMITTED: client_conversations has NO conversation/thread id (its PK is a per-MESSAGE bigint; grouping is only the tuple (client_id, user_email, surface, created_at)) — no clean key, so skipped rather than invented. CLASSIFIER = ONE source (src/lib/lora-family-classify.ts, used at WRITE time by lora-tool-log AND by scripts/lora-tool-decision-rate.mjs via isNarratedFamily): a NARRATED family (already in build-claude-context's prompt) → a from-context answer is CORRECT; a captured-history-only family → a from-context answer is the SKIP the rate measures; unclassifiable → 'unknown', EXCLUDED from the rate (never silently bucketed). INSTRUMENT (src/lib/lora-tool-log.ts) mirrors logSpend exactly (async · try/catch · swallows all · never throws), called FIRE-AND-FORGET (void, not awaited) per turn in runClaudeToolLoop — NO BEHAVIOR CHANGE (no tool_choice added, tools/system prompt untouched; the L2 measurement was 0/11 skip — we WATCH it, not change it). GATE-A (real path, real Opus, writes only the new table): (a) a real turn's logged row MATCHED the model's actual turn-0 decision (family='placement', tool_called + tool_name as observed); (b) with the table renamed away the same turn RETURNED normally — the PGRST205 insert error was console.error'd + swallowed, 0 rows written (proven, not asserted); (c) the rate split captured/narrated correctly over seeds (4/3 skip · 2/1 from-context); (d) the fire-and-forget dispatch adds 0.065 ms/turn on the response path (the insert lands AFTER the response). Migration applied (table empty); the code ships with this commit. | LORAMER_LORA_TOOL_DECISION_LOG_V1, 2026-07-23 | do not relitigate.
- [DECISION + VERIFIED 2026-07-23] **LORAMER_NEXT_CONV_WRITE_V1 — the -next chat now persists its turns to client_conversations; the redesign was a WRITE ISLAND.** THE ISLAND: dashboard-next mounts ONE chat (ChatLauncher in Shell) with ONE message thread, and it held turns only in React state — ZERO writers. So every -next conversation was invisible to Lora's cross-surface memory recap (/api/intelligence reads client_conversations), invisible to every other surface, and invisible to ★N5 export. Measured cost: the NEWEST client_conversations row before this fix was 2026-06-29 — writing had gone quiet on the legacy surfaces while real use moved to the write-island -next. FIX: both turns POST to the EXISTING /api/conversations (the same path legacy uses — NO new table, NO new endpoint, NO second write path) via one client-side writer src/lib/next/log-conversation-turn.ts. ONE SURFACE VALUE, not three per trigger: NEXT_CHAT_SURFACE='next-ask-lora' covers the pill, the mobile Lora tab, AND the drill-row ✦ because they are one mounted component / one thread — DEVICE IS NOT A SURFACE, and the per-surface Clear (DELETE is keyed by surface) would break if one visible conversation were fragmented across buckets. A drill-opened turn is marked on the EXISTING scope column (scope='drill'), snapshotted at turn start so both turns of the exchange share it — not a second surface. ASSISTANT TURNS ARE LOGGED ONLY ON A GENUINE REPLY (res.ok + d.response): the client-side fallback/error placeholders ("Something went wrong…", "Network error…") are NOT Lora's output and logging them would poison the recap. FAILURE POSTURE mirrors the L2 instrument EXACTLY — fire-and-forget: never awaited, wrapped in try/catch, the fetch rejection swallowed, never throws (legacy AWAITED these writes; this is strictly safer). NO BEHAVIOR CHANGE otherwise (messages array, /api/chat body, system prompt, tools, intelligence path all untouched). GATE-A (real writer fn · real DB · real recap query + real render, sentinels cleaned up): (a) the real writer emits BOTH POSTs with surface='next-ask-lora', correct role/scope/clientId/content, and send() wires user + assistant (assistant gated on res.ok+d.response), un-awaited; (b) with a FAILING fetch (async-reject AND sync-throw) the writer returns void and never throws → the turn's control flow is untouched; (c) a real -next user+assistant pair inserted for The Escential Group appeared in the EXACT intelligence recap query AND rendered into the system-prompt suffix under "PREVIOUS CONVERSATIONS WITH THIS USER" → a -next conversation reaches Lora's cross-surface memory; (d) MOBILE/sm — the writer has zero viewport refs and the mobile Lora tab reaches the same send() with no breakpoint guard, so a turn at sm writes identically (stated limit: no headless browser in the repo, so sm CSS layout was not pixel-asserted). | LORAMER_NEXT_CONV_WRITE_V1, 2026-07-23 | do not relitigate.
- [DIAGNOSIS 2026-07-24 — NOT FIXED, MECHANISM UNIDENTIFIED] **LORAMER_NEXT_CHAT_KEYBOARD_BLEED_V1 — the -next Ask-Lora sheet bleeds the page through when the on-screen KEYBOARD is OPEN; NO sixth fix without an identified mechanism.** SYMPTOM (Russ, 2026-07-24, screenshots): with the mobile keyboard raised, page content (ClientPage below) is visible BELOW the chat input bar — the fixed full-screen sheet does not cover the area the keyboard exposes. This reproduces WITH THE KEYBOARD OPEN specifically (distinct from the earlier keyboard-DISMISS pan and from the horizontal wide-answer overflow). CURRENT SHIPPED STATE (verified this session): `.scrim` is `position:fixed; inset:0; z-index:60`; `.panel` is `height:100dvh` at BOTH breakpoints; `visualViewport` is referenced ONLY by the `?debug=chat` readout (LORAMER_NEXT_CHAT_DEBUG_V1) — there is NO visualViewport→layout binding. NOT A STACKING-CONTEXT TRAP (verified this session): NONE of the scrim's ancestors (`.subheader` → `.main` → `.body` → `.root` → `<body>`) carries transform / filter / will-change / opacity<1 / backdrop-filter / contain / isolation / perspective (redesign.module.css contains none of them anywhere); the fixed z-index:60 scrim is a ROOT-level layer over static/auto-z page content, so the bleed is NOT a z-index/stacking problem. FIVE PRIOR ATTEMPTS (none fixed the keyboard bleed): (1) LORAMER_MOBILE_BOTTOM_SHEET_V1 (4707757) — legacy /dashboard mobile bottom sheet "preserves visible context"; SHIPPED (legacy surface, not -next). (2) popover bottom-sheet experiment (9af6c92 "never cropped") → REVERTED (1c7273c "breaks desktop"). (3) LORAMER_NEXT_CHAT_FLEX_MINWIDTH_V1 (25b4957) — min-width:0 down the flex chain + `.md` table/pre internal scrollers; SHIPPED; fixed the HORIZONTAL wide-answer overflow / send-arrow-off-screen, NOT the keyboard bleed. (4) LORAMER_NEXT_CHAT_VISUAL_VIEWPORT_V1 (78de5ab) — bound `.scrim` `--chat-h`/`--chat-top` to `window.visualViewport.height`/`.offsetTop` (100dvh fallback) and `.panel`→`height:100%` → REVERTED (e1bcf75, 2026-07-17), stated reason: "did NOT fix ★UI-OVERFLOW (unchanged on device, Chrome + Safari); an unproven change carried into launch week is pure risk." (5) LORAMER_NEXT_CHAT_DEBUG_V1 (130bae0 + 6cace15) — `?debug=chat` in-flow, peak-tracked horizontal-axis readout; SHIPPED; an INSTRUMENT to measure `visualViewport.offsetLeft`, NOT a fix. THE MECHANISM IS NOT YET IDENTIFIED. "dvh does not shrink for the keyboard" is a TRUE banked premise, but the one attempt that acted on it (the visualViewport binding, #4) did NOT fix the symptom on-device — so that premise is NECESSARY-NOT-SUFFICIENT and something else is in play; candidate axes NOT yet proven: iOS position:fixed behavior under the keyboard, the sheet's own scroll/overflow, the `env(safe-area-inset-bottom)` input-bar padding, or a mis-identification of what "bleed" actually shows. RULE: NO SIXTH ATTEMPT until the mechanism is identified AND reproduced — five undirected attempts across two sessions is the signature of guessing (cross-ref the RULE-HOME LAW: repeat failure needs an identified cause, not another try). NEXT STEP IS A MEASUREMENT (with the keyboard OPEN: which element is visible, at what coordinates, against visualViewport vs layout viewport) BEFORE any code. This entry RECORDS the diagnosis; it fixes nothing. Cross-ref QUEUE ★UI-OVERFLOW / ★CHAT-GATE-ZINDEX (distinct symptoms). | LORAMER_NEXT_CHAT_KEYBOARD_BLEED_V1, 2026-07-24 | do not relitigate.
- [DECISION + VERIFIED 2026-07-24] **LORAMER_AGENCY_SCOPE_LORA_V1 — agency / all-clients Lora gets tools + per-call RBAC (was tool-less and printed "Platform: undefined").** THE DEFECT (recon this session): at the all-clients Shell, clientId is empty → the tool gate `clientId && viewerCanAccess(...)` withheld ALL tools (Lora could query nothing), and the fallback prompt rendered `Platform: ${platform}` as the literal "Platform: undefined" (platform is destructured off the request body with no default and -next never sends it). THE RULE (Russ, 2026-07-24, destination — do not re-ask): a question that NAMES a client → Lora answers it using that client's data; a GENERIC question → she asks which client (or says to click into one). CROSS-CLIENT questions ("which client had the best ROAS") are NOT covered by this rule and REMAIN the Agency Lora tier in docs/LORAMER_LORA_SPEC.md — this is the near-term slice, NOT a closed door. THE BUILD (5 parts): (1) route.ts destructures `platform = ''` and the single-client fallback OMITS the Platform clause entirely when absent — never renders "undefined". (2) claude-tools.ts tool gate is now `userEmail ? [tools] : undefined` (the clientId-presence gate is REMOVED) so tools attach at agency scope. (3) RBAC IS EXPLICIT + PER CALL, server-side, in the runClaudeToolLoop EXECUTOR: for every tool_use it resolves the TARGET client = the bound scope client (single-client tab — wins, and the model cannot steer it off) OR, at agency scope, the model-supplied `tu.input.clientId`; then `viewerCanAccess(userEmail, target)` runs and FAILS CLOSED (no target OR no access → an is_error tool_result, the query layer is never reached). This per-call check is now the ONLY thing preventing cross-client access, which is why it lives at the point of use, not at tool-attach time. (4) the agency prompt (buildAgencyScopeContext) carries the RBAC-SCOPED roster (listAccessibleClientsWithNames — reuses listAccessibleClients' owner∪org-grant∪legacy precedence + archived-drop, then names; it can never widen the set) so Lora can resolve a named client — and ONLY clients this viewer can access. (5) each query tool gained an optional `clientId` param (REQUIRED at agency scope, IGNORED at single-client scope). GATE-A (real DB RBAC, real identities, real Opus for the model-behavior cases; query layer a light real client-scoped read; zero writes): (a) agency+OWNER names "The Escential Group" → REAL Opus resolved it to c39ee088 and the executor queried THAT client, answered; (b) agency+generic "how did we do last month?" → REAL Opus called NO tool and asked which client ("Which client would you like me to look at?"); (c) SECURITY, REAL non-owner cote.russell@gmail.com (a real org member granted ONLY Foam OH) forces a query_metrics for Escential c39ee088 → executor's viewerCanAccess DENIES (real resolveAccess → null) → is_error "Access denied", the query layer NEVER touched that client (no leak); (d) the roster for that partial member is EXACTLY [Foam OH], not the owner's other 19 clients; (e) single-client scope unchanged — the bound client is queried and a model-supplied clientId param does NOT steer it off the bound client. tsc 0. WHAT NO STATIC GATE PROVES: that Lora always WORDS the resolve-or-ask correctly — the prompt gives her the rule + the RBAC-scoped roster; the wording is the eval set's question. | LORAMER_AGENCY_SCOPE_LORA_V1, 2026-07-24 | do not relitigate.
- [DECISION 2026-07-24 — LAW, Russ's rule not a proposal] **LORAMER_L4_DETERMINISM_LAW_V1 — L4 determinism = same data + same question → same CONCLUSION, not same wording.** THE DEFINITION: on UNCHANGED data, the same question must reach the same CLAIM. PROSE IS FREE TO VARY; the claim is NOT. The gate tests for CONTRADICTION — opposite DIRECTION, a DIFFERENT entity named as the problem, a threshold crossed differently — NOT identical wording. Two answers can differ and BOTH be right (cut one campaign vs cut two) — that is NOT a failure; only a contradiction is. PREREQUISITE (load-bearing): the JUDGMENT BASIS must be fixed in DATA first — value_model, targets, thresholds. A determinism test over UNSTABLE ground measures the GROUND, not the model — an unset value_model makes "is this ROAS good" non-reproducible BY CONSTRUCTION (see QUEUE ★VALUE-MODEL-COVERAGE-GAP: 11 of 28 active clients have no value_model). This is the L4 rung of the LORA-COMPLETENESS arc; the instrument that will test it is QUEUE ★LORA-DETERMINISM-HARNESS — it does NOT exist yet: the shipped tests/lora-evals/run-evals.mjs (now `npm run evals`) is SINGLE-run-vs-fixed-expectation, and the 2026-07-15 "3-pass, zero flips" result was OPERATOR-eyeballed across three manual runs, not code. | LORAMER_L4_DETERMINISM_LAW_V1, 2026-07-24 | do not relitigate.

- ⚠️ GOOGLE CLIENT-SECRET CLEANUP — **POST-VERIFICATION ONLY. - SIGN-IN ASKS EVERY USER FOR ADWORDS — auth.ts:23 sends `openid email profile https://www.googleapis.com/auth/adwords` on EVERY login, so a Shopify/GA-only business owner is asked to approve "See, edit, create, and delete your Google Ads accounts" BEFORE connecting anything. An onboarding/trust problem (worst consent copy in the product, shown to 100% of signups) and it widens the sensitive-scope surface for users who will never touch Google Ads. Fix = decouple adwords from LOGIN (the F3 decoupler route pair already proves the pattern — capture adwords POST-login, on demand); login keeps only openid/email/profile. Own flight, NOT a same-day change: it touches auth.ts (the login path) and the consent screen's scope set → Lesson 42 re-verification. Sequence it AFTER the GA verification clears. src: 2026-07-15 OAuth scope enumeration. open [LC]
- DUPLICATE CLIENT-NAME TRAP — there are TWO clients named "Influential Drones": 5bb9b2ff-a1df-4d46-ac6b-0471ef543e15 (Google Ads + GA) and 2617b163-f392-427e-9a29-f134acc51406 (Ads only, no GA). Any instruction naming a client by NAME ALONE is ambiguous and a destructive/connect action on the wrong one is silent. CARRY THE UUID in any instruction that acts on a client. Cheap guard worth building: warn on duplicate client names per owner at create time. src: 2026-07-15 GA/Ads connection audit. open [LC]

This is the STRUCTURE half of the asset layer — M-FILL#1's seven asset breakdowns are the PERFORMANCE half and are already shipped. ⚠ IT DOES NOT BELONG IN metrics_daily: it has NO date, NO spend and NO metric, so forcing it into a daily metrics table means INVENTING a date for a thing that has none — the capture inventory already calls it "the asset content layer (creative store, not metrics_daily)". - ★ META SKAN / COARSE_CONVERSION_VALUE (M7) — ON-DEMAND, deliberately NOT built. breakdowns=skan_conversion_id is iOS APP-INSTALL attribution; NOT ONE CLIENT IN THE COHORT RUNS APP-INSTALL CAMPAIGNS, so building it now costs a report per lap to capture guaranteed-empty data for everyone. - ★ META-BACKFILL-OBSERVED-ZERO — FLEET-WIDE, not one client. FORWARD and BACKFILL disagree about what a dormant day looks like. Forward (meta-metrics-row.ts) pushes the account row UNCONDITIONALLY from totals, so a dormant account still gets a daily $0 anchor row. Backfill (fetchMetaDailyMetrics → runBackfill) writes ONLY the days Meta returns, so a dormant stretch walked by backfill produces NO rows. Same day, two different truths depending on which path saw it. CONSEQUENCES, both observed 2026-07-19: (1) it is why Influential Drones' dormant stretch holds zero rows once forward broke — backfill could never have covered for it; (2) it makes the standard-C landing gate's PARTITIONING anchor untrustworthy, because "an account row exists" stops meaning "we looked at this day" (the false Ennis flag this morning came from an anchor that included days no breakdown could ever exist for). FIX, SCOPED NOT AUTHORED: make Meta backfill emit a $0 account row for days Meta returns empty, matching forward's observed-zero. This is NOT a fabricated zero and does NOT violate the false-zero law — it records the SAME observed-empty that forward already records; the distinction is observed-empty (Meta answered, nothing ran) vs invented (we never asked). BLAST RADIUS: the SHARED backfill path (run-backfill.ts + the meta adapter), so every platform riding that engine must be read first — a read-first scope pass before any authoring, no exceptions. src: 2026-07-19 Meta unseal recon. open [LC]
- ★ LANDING-GATE-WIRING DEPENDENCY — wire the standard-C landing gate (scripts/check-capture-landing.mjs, untracked at a8db2e6) AFTER M-FILL#8, never before. The gate's PARTITIONING standard measures breakdown coverage against account-grain anchor days; until dormant days are consistent between forward and backfill, that anchor produces false gaps and the gate would cry wolf on its first wired run. Ordering is the whole point of this entry. src: 2026-07-19 standard-C build + Meta unseal recon. open [LC]

- ★ THIRD-PARTY-ATTRIBUTION-OVERLAY PRINCIPLE (banked 2026-07-19, Russ) — tools like Triple Whale sit OVER the same platform APIs we already read and sell an ATTRIBUTION MODEL on top. Two consequences we hold as principle, not preference: (a) the raw capture layer is OURS and is the harder, more durable asset — an overlay cannot answer a question the underlying capture never stored, which is exactly why the capture-everything law is the moat; (b) when we DO add an attribution model, it must be a LABELLED, SWAPPABLE LAYER over untouched raw rows — never a rewrite of what we captured. Cross-ref the read-layer-projection-only architecture used for the Meta alias canonicalization: raw rows stay untouched forever. src: 2026-07-19 strategy conversation. open [NP]
- ★ COHORT-PRIVACY-DOCS — 🚨 LAUNCH BLOCKER, opened 2026-07-19. The WooCommerce customer_cohort feature (LORAMER_WOO_COHORT_V1) PROCESSES CUSTOMER EMAIL to derive lifetime-order buckets. The engineering posture is already the safe one — sha256 computed in memory, discarded when the pass returns, nothing identifying written to metrics_daily, and nested field trimming means we never even RECEIVE name/phone/address — but the legal surface is not the code. BEFORE ANY REAL MERCHANT USES THIS FEATURE we owe: (1) a Privacy Policy "Merchant/Customer Data" section, and (2) a DPA establishing LoraMer as PROCESSOR and the merchant as CONTROLLER, stating that the merchant owns customer consent, that identity is a transient hash never stored, and that data is deleted on termination. Needs its OWN drafting flight plus lawyer review — NOT drafted tonight, and explicitly not something to improvise. Until it exists, treat cohort as internal-only. src: 2026-07-19 wrap. open [LC]

- ★LORA-CROSS-SURFACE-HISTORY — VIOLATES the banked one-continuous-mind law in docs/LORAMER_LORA_SPEC.md. chat/route.ts:28 takes `history` from the request BODY and builds messages at :142-143; it NEVER queries client_conversations. So Lora's turn-by-turn memory is the CURRENT browser tab only — not prior sessions, devices, or surfaces. Partial mitigation: the intelligence profile carries a SEPARATE `conversations` field (a different injection than the messages history), contents UNREAD as of 2026-07-23 — read it before scoping the fix. - ★LORA-CLIENT-RESOLUTION-DETERMINISM — at agency scope (LORAMER_AGENCY_SCOPE_LORA_V1) the MODEL resolves a client the user names to an id. Per the DETERMINISM LAW (the model never DECIDES, only REPORTS), resolution should happen IN CODE: an EXACT match against the RBAC-scoped roster answers; an AMBIGUOUS or NO match ASKS which client. RBAC is unaffected either way — the executor still viewerCanAccess-checks the resolved target — this is about two similarly-named clients producing a QUESTION instead of a confident WRONG answer. Belongs in the T4 Lora-completeness arc. src: 2026-07-24 agency-scope build. open [LC]
- ★LORA-RESULT-CACHE — every Lora turn is a full Opus call with NO result reuse: the SAME question, SAME client, and NO new captured data still re-derives from scratch. Prompt caching covers only the stable PREFIX, not the answer. MARGIN item — Business is $99 for 750 questions, so repeated identical turns eat the margin. The cache KEY must include a DATA-VERSION STAMP so a new capture invalidates it; that stamp LIKELY SHARES A DESIGN with the queued latest-date-from-watermark item (cross-ref the latest-date/watermark work). src: 2026-07-24 cost/margin review. open [LC]
- ★L4-DETERMINISM (T4 Lora-completeness arc) — LAW banked DECISIONS LORAMER_L4_DETERMINISM_LAW_V1 (Russ 2026-07-24, not a proposal): same data + same question → same CONCLUSION, not same wording. The gate tests for CONTRADICTION (opposite direction / a different entity named as the problem / a threshold crossed differently), NEVER identical text; two answers can differ and both be right (cut 1 vs cut 2 campaigns) — that is not a failure. BLOCKED-BY: the judgment basis must be fixed in DATA first (value_model / targets / thresholds — ★VALUE-MODEL-COVERAGE-GAP); a determinism test over unstable ground measures the ground, not the model. INSTRUMENT = ★LORA-DETERMINISM-HARNESS. src: 2026-07-24 L4 recon + Russ's rule. open [LC]
- ★LORA-DETERMINISM-HARNESS — NEW instrument (does not exist): run the SAME question TWICE against UNCHANGED data and compare CLAIMS, not text — a contradiction (opposite direction / different entity blamed / threshold crossed differently) FAILS; prose variance is fine. Today's tests/lora-evals/run-evals.mjs (now `npm run evals`) is SINGLE-run-vs-fixed-expectation, and the 2026-07-15 "3-pass, zero flips" was OPERATOR-eyeballed across three manual runs, not code. Cost ~$8–10 per run-twice pass at current Opus rates. Depends on the judgment basis being fixed first (★VALUE-MODEL-COVERAGE-GAP) or it measures the ground. src: 2026-07-24 L4 recon. open [LC]

- ★ G2.7 — THE TAIL (rank past topN) — **POST-LAUNCH.** Lora can RANK but not REACH past topN (clamp [1,50], no offset); for search_term the rows are already in lambda memory and discarded. TWO ASKS, DIFFERENT SHAPES: · FILTER (the real build) — "what's wasting money" = spend>0 AND conversions=0, ranked; RANK-INDEPENDENT (the biggest waste is often #1 — Escential's "essential oils" $155 / 34 clicks / 0 conv sits at the top), no paging needed. · OFFSET (cheap, rides along) — LIMIT/OFFSET on the bounded path, array slice on the unbounded path. ⚠ VOLUME FLOOR REQUIRED: zero-conversions catches dead terms AND terms with 2 clicks that never had a chance — naming those is confidently-wrong advice, same class as the Display hour-0 midnight bid-down. - ★ G2.5 — GEO ABSENCE DIAGNOSIS ("where am I blind?") — **POST-LAUNCH, ordered AFTER ★G2.** WHY: Lora can say what happened somewhere; she CANNOT say where NOTHING happened. Absence is never served by any platform — Google returns zero rows for zero-activity geos (banked 2026-06-28; NOT a false-zero bug, correct behavior). Absence must therefore be COMPUTED at question-time: targeted universe MINUS observed rows.
- ★ G2.6 — DENOMINATOR LAYER (cross-cutting normalization; NOT a geo feature) — **POST-LAUNCH, ordered AFTER ★G2; does NOT gate G2 or G2.5.** WHY — THE MOAT CASE: GA says Wyoming sends high organic traffic; Google says zero impressions there. "Demand exists and you are not buying it" is multi-source-provenance law at its sharpest — the value is explaining WHY sources disagree, and presence-vs-absence is the sharpest disagreement. Same shape for Shopify conversion rate by state, GA sessions, Google impressions. Any geo dimension can borrow it.

- ★ CHAT-STREAMING — stream /api/chat responses token-by-token to the -next chat (ChatLauncher) instead of awaiting the whole answer. THE DURABLE FIX for slow turns: a 59s answer that renders progressively is ALIVE; a 59s spinner is DEAD (2026-07-24 a real turn ran ~59s server-side, returned 200, but the browser had already given up and the user saw a failure for an answer that existed). Claude-app-caliber mobile behavior is the STANDARD (already banked). Shape: switch the Anthropic call to a stream, return an incremental response (SSE / ReadableStream) from /api/chat, and render deltas as they arrive — the tool loop's intermediate turns can surface a "working…" state instead of a dead spinner. - ★ DEPLOY-WEBHOOK — **RESOLVED (transient); STAYS OPEN pending recurrence.** WHAT HAPPENED (history, keep it): 2026-07-16 ~21:10Z git-push deployment CREATION silently stopped — commits be58a07 and 9b14d16 pushed cleanly to origin/main but Vercel created NO deployment record in ANY state (not canceled, not errored, not queued; 543d315 at 21:10:45Z was the last git-created deploy, READY). RESOLUTION: **NOT broken — a transient webhook delivery/processing failure.** Vercel support confirmed from their side: no deployment records existed for be58a07/9b14d16, project config was correct throughout (gitProviderOptions.createDeployments enabled, production branch main, no git.deploymentEnabled:false), and git deploys resumed after the CLI deploy. CONFIRMED BY OBSERVATION (commit 25b4957): the deploy was created BY THE GIT INTEGRATION (source=git) — the trigger works; Vercel also FLUSHED THE BACKLOG (be58a07, 9b14d16, ac5e6b9, a06d68e each got their own git-created deployment, all READY). So it was a DELAYED webhook queue that recovered, not a permanent break. **NO manual CLI step is required going forward.** The one-time CLI deploy (dpl_HqiUCbJhr4fZ9D4S7cEKD7AnNdUh, 9b14d16 tree) was the unblock, not a standing workaround. STAYS OPEN: watch the next several commits — a one-off delay and a systemic fault look identical from inside one incident. If it recurs, the Vercel case is open with the SHAs (be58a07, 9b14d16) + the 2026-07-16T21:10:45Z boundary. THE LAW STANDS REGARDLESS: DECISIONS "A PUSH IS NOT A DEPLOY" — every local gate read green while prod served old code and nothing in the pipeline noticed; confirm a deployment EXISTS and reads READY against the expected commit before handing Russ any Gate-B check. src: 2026-07-16 deploy-integration diagnosis + Vercel support. open-watch [LC]
- ★ SUPPORT-BOT — **POST-LAUNCH, NOT before 2026-07-22.** THE MODEL (Vercel's support bot, 2026-07-16): it answered "what happened to MY project" by reading Russ's ACTUAL deployment history, his createDeployments flag, his production branch — not documentation. It confirmed our diagnosis independently, named PRECISELY where its access ended (webhook delivery logs are not self-service), offered a human, then drafted the support case PRE-FILLED with everything it already knew — leaving Russ only the two things it could NOT infer: which project + the deployment URL. THE LESSON: ask ONLY what you cannot look up; every support form that makes a user retype what the system already knows is a form that never read its own database. SCOPE — SMALLER THAN LORA, NOT BIGGER: Lora does open-ended analysis over millions of rows across five platforms and explains why sources disagree; a support bot answers a narrow, mostly-CLOSED set — is my connection healthy, why is my data missing, when did my backfill last run, why is this number different from the platform's. Those are LOOKUPS against state that already exists: platform_connections.health / last_ok_at / last_error_code, sync_state cursors + backfill_complete, the __google_quota sentinel, cron_runs. Same architectural shape as query_metrics (tools over the DB, scoped to the caller); different tables, different skill doc — the hard part is already built. TWO/THREE THINGS THAT DECIDE GOOD vs LIABILITY: (1) SCOPING IS THE WHOLE GAME — Vercel's bot saw Russ's project and ONLY Russ's project; a LoraMer support bot reading connection health must be ORG-SCOPED AT THE TOOL LAYER, not by prompt. The org spine exists (RBAC, migration 027 org_id NOT-NULL) but this is the FIRST tool that reads PLUMBING rather than metrics — treat it as a new RBAC surface, not a new prompt. (2) IT MUST SAY "I DON'T KNOW" — name the exact edge of its access and hand off; a bot that invents a cause for a broken connection is WORSE than no bot (the user acts on it). Same law as LORA_SPEC's settled-vs-contested calibration: confident wrongness is the liability. (3) ESCALATION SHAPE — when it cannot answer, draft the ticket PRE-FILLED and ask only for what it cannot infer; LoraMer's analogue of Vercel's "deployment URL" is which client / which date range / which platform — everything else (connection health, cursor position, last sync, quota state) it already has. src: 2026-07-16 Vercel support-bot model. open [LC]

- ★ INSIGHT-INVESTIGATOR — the insight bar is a REBUILD, not a model swap (post ★OPUS-EVERYWHERE; deliberate speed, behind the 07-16 unfinished work). Roadmapped 2026-06-10 as the While-You-Were-Sleeping digest: every metric with meaningful overnight movement, each with a specific recommendation + a connecting overall-strategy explanation. Russ 07-17: it must answer WHY — not "you spent more last night" but "because <search term> ate $X" or "a spike from <city>, TX." THAT IS A TOOL LOOP, not a completion: detect → drill (query_metrics then query_breakdown, iteratively — the same loop chat runs on a "why" question). Haiku cannot drive a tool loop — the real reason the model decision was never a blurb-quality question. ONLY POSSIBLE SINCE 2026-07-16: until G2 closed, Lora could not reach geo / GA dimensional / age_gender — the "why" data was captured and UNREADABLE; now 118/118. THREE DESIGN CONSTRAINTS, each a way this ships BROKEN: (1) ATTRIBUTION IS NOT SHARE — the anomaly is a delta against ITS OWN baseline, not its share of the total; naive top-N names the biggest line item every night and trains users to ignore the bar. (2) A CAPTURE HOLE LOOKS EXACTLY LIKE A COLLAPSE — G1 froze Meta breadth 17 days; a detector running then would have screamed "conversions dropped to zero" every morning (false-zero law on the most-read surface in the app); the detector MUST distinguish NO DATA from ZERO → it needs reconcile/capture state, not just metrics. (3) SPLIT THE MATH FROM THE PROSE — detection is deterministic (thresholds, baselines, code); Lora EXPLAINS what the math found (preserves the determinism law; stops the model DECIDING what is anomalous, which is where hallucinated urgency comes from). ⚠ COST STOPS BEING TRIVIAL HERE — but of the DESTINATION, not today: when built this becomes a multi-turn investigation per client per day = the highest-frequency call in the product AT THE DESTINATION (N clients daily); the CURRENT insight call is near-ZERO (legacy-cohort only, below). Model the cost BEFORE building. ⚠ CORRECTED 2026-07-17 — THIS IS A BUILD, NOT AN UPGRADE TO A LIVE SURFACE: the proactive insight surface DOES NOT EXIST on -next (MultiClientOverview.tsx:184 is a neutral "Proactive insights … coming soon" placeholder; the real banner lives ONLY in the legacy dashboard, page.tsx:1415/:1523, and middleware.ts:33-38 redirects every non-legacy-cohort user away from it — VERIFIED; anthropic_spend_log last-7-days had ZERO organic insight calls, only a Shopify reviewer fixture). So ★INSIGHT-INVESTIGATOR = build the -next banner ITSELF + the precompute engine + the schedule, from the placeholder up — not an upgrade to a running surface. The Opus floor (★OPUS-EVERYWHERE) is already correct and waiting for it. src: roadmap 2026-06-10 + Russ 2026-07-17. open [LC]
- ★ DIGEST-WINDOW-MODEL — the SETTLED shape (Russ 2026-07-17) for the While-You-Were-Sleeping digest's WINDOW + SCHEDULING. · TIMEZONE IS A PROPERTY OF THE CLIENT: "while THEY slept" = their overnight on THEIR clock; a Pacific client's window is Pacific even when the agency is Eastern. · THE SCHEDULE IS A PROPERTY OF THE READER: the agency opens the app at THEIR 6am and everything computed so far is sitting there — NO per-client-morning fan-out scheduler is needed; each window computes on its own clock and surfaces whenever the reader looks. A Pacific client's 7pm-7am ends at 10am ET, so it is NOT ready at 6am ET — a fact about the earth, not a bug; Lora STATES it ("Pacific clients through 7am PT, ready ~10am ET") per the honesty law. · THE WINDOW IS DIRECTABLE: default 7pm-7am local, overridable per client, with an agency-level default new clients inherit — a settings field + a client-profile field, NOT new architecture. · WHAT EXISTS (VERIFIED 2026-07-17): organizations carries only (id, name, owner_email, org_type, created_at) — no timezone, no logo, no settings PAGE anywhere; client_context IS the business-context page already (ClientPage.tsx → /api/context); NO timezone column in ANY table. · TIMEZONE IS DERIVABLE, NOT ASKABLE, FOR MOST: google-ads.ts:26,35 ALREADY fetches customer_client.time_zone into the live intelligence and throws it away; Shopify exposes shop.iana_timezone and we never ask; Meta uses advertiser TZ for hour buckets and we store the label, not the zone. Derive first; the settings page is the human override. · THE INTERPRETATION JOB, not the scheduling job: platform hours are reported in the ACCOUNT's timezone — a Pacific client's "22:00" is the agency's 01:00; converting platform hours to the client's real clock is what makes an overnight window MEAN anything (that is why the account timezone matters — NOT for firing a cron). · CARDINALITY (Russ's model confirmed, mine corrected): ONE org + N client_contexts for BOTH agency and owner; nothing constrains an owner to one client (one 'business' account already has two) — same shape, different convention, NOT two page types. src: Russ 2026-07-17. open [LC]
- ★ HOUR-GRAIN-CAPTURE-HOLE — launch-relevant; VIOLATES ESSENCE (capture everything, FULL GRAIN). VERIFIED 2026-07-17: Google + Meta store hour grain; Shopify, WooCommerce, and GA DO NOT — and it is OUR choice, not a platform limit. Shopify's Admin API returns order createdAt to the SECOND; our writer aggregates to a daily row and DISCARDS the timestamp. Woo the same. GA4 exposes an hour dimension; we capture 12 GA dimensional types and NONE is hourly. ⇒ "Someone ordered at 3am" — the single most interesting sentence an overnight digest could say — is UNANSWERABLE because we threw the timestamp away. A direct violation of CAPTURE EVERYTHING / FULL GRAIN. THREE WRITERS, not three platforms (Shopify + Woo + GA hour capture). src: 2026-07-17 verify. open [LC]
- ★ PLATFORM-SURFACE-AUDIT — for EACH of the five platforms, enumerate FROM THE PLATFORM'S OWN DOCS every field, dimension, and grain the API OFFERS; diff against what metrics_daily holds; report the delta. Reference = the VENDOR'S docs, NEVER our writers/inventory/registry (see DECISIONS "EVERY AUDIT SO FAR COMPARED US TO OURSELVES"). This is the audit the other three should have been: the capture audits + the 2026-07-11 parity audit compared us to ourselves; G2 (07-16) found 118 captured-but-UNREADABLE tuples (the READ side) — this checks the WRITE side (offered-but-never-fetched, e.g. the hour-grain hole above). Sized honestly: five platforms, real work. src: 2026-07-17. ✅ COMPLETE 2026-07-18 — ALL 5 PLATFORMS DIFFED, vendor-sourced (results → docs/LORAMER_DATA_COMPLETENESS.md: one "## <platform> — PLATFORM-SURFACE-AUDIT RESULT" section per platform [Google/Meta/Shopify/Woo/GA4] + the CROSS-PLATFORM PATTERNS block). EMAIL identity instead (guests are 86% of orders, so registered-only would have been 86% UNKNOWN) → UNKNOWN came out 0.00% and repeat customers are 55% of the real store's net.

WOO-SPECIFIC: date_created carries NO offset, so the value is date_created_gmt normalised to UTC with both verbatim strings in extra; the row date stays the SITE-LOCAL day (re-keying to GMT would shift rows across midnight and break 7.5yr idempotency).

## I. LESSONS INDEX 1–60 (+ dated)  (source: LORAMER_DECISIONS.md)
1 Silent-skip via shared marker — use content-based idempotency, not marker-presence.
2 Scope assumption in destructure adds — grep the prop in the parent's scope before patching.
3 TS prop add = two edits/component (destructure AND type; check inline vs multi-line type).
4 JS string apostrophes break builds — use backticks for any string with apostrophes/quotes.
5 Stale anchors — re-read the current file (fresh sed/grep) before any patch.
6 Marker-collision silent failure — distinct sub-markers OR per-edit content checks.
7 Per-edit content-based idempotency check is the best practice (all/some/none present logic).
8 Silent .catch(()=>[]) hides GAQL/API errors — instrument console.error before concluding "no data".
9 Cache invalidation hides deployed fixes (15-min) — force a miss via a never-used date range.
10 Whitespace in anchors — bytes matter; dump exact bytes when an anchor fails.
11 PROMPT-AS-MIRROR — grounding/constraint text goes in code comments (INTERNAL_GROUNDING), never user-rendered prompt.
12 Meta breakdowns go in &breakdowns=, NOT &fields= (else HTTP 400, swallowed by .catch).
13 Same-line comment after a token (comma/paren/bracket/template) can break webpack — comment on its own line.
14 tsc --noEmit is NOT npm run build — webpack is stricter (syntax/mangled-literals); build is the real gate.
15 Surfacing raw API status/body into the prompt = diagnostic of last resort (always with a planned cleanup).
16 Anchor only from the current-turn paste — never memory/earlier turns/grep; small anchors over big.
17 Same-named files + blind mv is dangerous — unique-name downloads before moving.
18 Patch scripts with hardcoded machine paths silently fail — match the machine's path.
19 ONE canonical date resolver (resolveDateWindow) — never roll per-platform date math.
20 Revenue = NET (currentSubtotalPriceSet), not gross — surface refunds; match merchant analytics.
21 GAQL has NO LAST_90_DAYS enum — explicit BETWEEN via resolveDateWindow.
22 Platform selector and tab nav are separate controls — switch to Overview on platform change from a non-ad tab.
23 Safe Supabase dup cleanup — backup→repoint children→verify counts→delete only emptied twins (keeper isn't always older).
24 Bug hunts in big files — investigate-only first, then a tight fix spec.
25 Repo is single source of truth — git pull at session start on either machine; unpushed work doesn't travel.
26a Serverless backfill cross-request cursor race — do the whole job in ONE invocation (in-memory loop); persist the cursor only for resume-after-interrupt, never as the loop's control.
26b RightPanel renders TWIN desktop/mobile message containers (hidden md:flex / flex md:hidden, both in DOM) — audit BOTH when touching either; assign anchors by document order. (HANDOFF dual-numbered both as "26"; HANDOFF:730 explicitly notes the collision.)
27 zsh eats unquoted globs (quote --include="*.ts"); BSD grep needs -E for alternation.
28 Verify a freshly-deployed cron/route against LIVE prod + give it time (stale triggers/logs mislead).
29 Heredoc/terminal pastes drop characters — deliver code as files; tsc catches mangled identifiers, NOT mangled string literals — grep critical strings.
30 Backfill depth = "as deep as the platform serves," discovered by probing; report the ACTUAL earliest row, never the swept cursor.
31 Per-platform retention differs — probe before trusting any documented limit.
32 JSX comments are {/* */}, not /* */ (renders as visible text; tsc misses it).
33 CRON-GATED VERIFICATION — deploy before the cron window or manually trigger after; capture writes YESTERDAY's date.
34 Handoffs anchor on session TAG + files, never a commit hash (local commits squash/rewrite on push).
35 pg_dump in CI: invoke by ABSOLUTE path /usr/lib/postgresql/17/bin/pg_dump (PATH resolves to v16).
36 GitHub Actions "Re-run jobs" replays the ORIGINAL commit — use a fresh workflow_dispatch to test a fix.
37 Vercel env rotation needs a redeploy to bind; native cron rotates atomically with the redeploy.
38 Supabase DB password is reset-safe (app uses API keys, not raw Postgres password).
39 A DB write that must touch a row → UPSERT (not UPDATE) + check affected count, log loudly on 0; never assume success on no-throw.
40 Never render internal flag/enum/status/tier keys to users — pass through a human-label map next to the keys.
41 Stripe Portal "cancel at period end" sets cancel_at (timestamp), not cancel_at_period_end (boolean).
42 Google OAuth consent-screen edits (name/domains/scopes/URLs/logo) trigger RE-verification — treat as frozen at launch.
43 Google Ads permissible-use update → Tool Change Form (zero-risk MCC metadata), not a full Standard Access app.
44 Walk every onboarding identity SHAPE with a real identity before launch (founder-only testing only exercises one shape).
45 vercel env pull can report a populated prod var as blank — verify "empty env" against runtime behavior; never re-set to a guess.
46 An API probe verifies what the CREDENTIAL can see, not what EXISTS — a boundary coinciding with a known limit IS the explanation; scope-truncated $0 rows are false-zeros, delete them.
47 EVERYTHING GETS EVERYTHING — completeness is a CORRECTNESS requirement; every gap explicit; any cap is a logged deliberate decision (MATRIX).
48 Vercel MCP has NO env-write — rotate via CLI (value via stdin, never printed) + redeploy to bind.
49 Guard NOT-NULL numerics vs NaN at the WRITE BOUNDARY (Number.isFinite), not per-builder (NaN ?? 0 = NaN → 23502 drops the whole row).
50 Don't conclude a logic bug from a symptom seen under one timing — replay the exact query against live DB; schedule catchup AFTER forward.
51 A backfill DRIVER LOOP must circuit-break on a persistent per-window error; never oscillate/re-walk; be gentle on live stores; resume from the TRUE frontier; when in doubt, STOP and surface.
52 Next.js App Router caches global fetch → deterministic supabase-js reads/writes go STALE/DROPPED on Vercel; force-no-store on read-after-write routes; a unique request body masks the bug.
53 A persisted UI selection carried across a context switch must be RE-VALIDATED against the new context (derive caps from the incoming entity); land on a valid non-blank default.
54 Shopify managed-install scopes come from the DEPLOYED config (shopify app deploy), not the authorize-URL scope= param; a refresh preserves the original grant; verify a scope change by PROBE.
55 A flag-gated reconnect control can be invisible exactly when needed — any re-auth/extend-scope affordance must be reachable for a HEALTHY connection.
56 shopify app deploy needs the Shopify CLI on node ≥22.12 (CLI 4.x crashes on node 20).
57 Vercel env VALUES are unreadable from tooling (masked / pull-blanked / no MCP env tool) — confirm from the source system.
58 Shopify revenue basis differs BY GRAIN — reconcile to the cent (per-line refund attribution + pro-rata residual) or ship a silent per-SKU lie; a WRONG basis is worse than no basis.
59 A permanent-history backfill must self-reconcile per unit of work (Σ within 1¢ each day BEFORE write/cursor-advance) or HALT loudly — never persist a bad day.
60 A connection-state claim (broken/dead/frozen/blocked/unhealthy/reconnect-needed) is a HYPOTHESIS until a LIVE capture-path probe proves it — never written as fact from a stored flag (health/last_error_code/oauth_190/last_ok_at) alone; stored flags are DERIVED CONTEXT, not ground truth (same class as the Google end_date adapter-semantics bug). Origin: a prior session wrote "Influential Drones Meta BLOCKED/broken/oauth_190" into CONTINUE_HERE + QUEUE + a session log as settled fact from the flag alone — it was FALSE (token alive HTTP 200, warehouse reconciled to the penny) and survived days because each session read it forward without re-deriving. RULE: before writing any negative connection claim into ANY handoff doc, run a live probe (raw HTTP status + body, Lesson 15 style); until probed, record "flag says X — UNVERIFIED, probe before acting," never as a blocker. The transient-190-dark-flags-a-live-connection generator = WS2 #2 (separate fix).
61 A backfill writer must STOP AT its retention floor as an EMPTY SUCCESS (per-adapter granularMonths clamp — meta=36, GA fixed 2015-08-14, Google account/dim 132mo), NOT overshoot into a boundary THROW; a step is 'done' ONLY on empty-success-at-floor or reconciled-to-floor, NEVER on an error. Origin: the onboarding drain's Meta account step stoppedOnError at the ~37mo boundary (it overshot to 132mo), never completed, and BLOCKED the later placement step. Fix (LORAMER_ONBOARD_DRAIN_V1): granularMonths=36 for meta; PER-STEP-INDEPENDENT drain (a stuck early step never starves a later one); verified Meta taxonomy decides done-vs-retry-vs-surface ({1,2,4,17,613,80004}/429/timeout=retry · 100·1487534=narrow-the-window · 100-other/190/368=surface · empty-success=done); NEVER swallow the fetch error (L15) — surface code/subcode so floor-vs-transient is distinguishable.
62 A platform-wide "stall" + a cluster of serverless TIMEOUTS with NO DB/lock/deadlock evidence and NO code-deploy correlation = look UPSTREAM at the external API's QUOTA, not infra. The 2026-06-28 Google 504 cluster (06:20–11:40Z) AND the 4h geo "stall" were ONE event: Basic-Access developer-scope quota exhaustion (15k ops/day, one shared dev token) burned by the morning geo fan-out by ~11:32Z. FALSIFIED, explicitly: (a) Supabase swap/memory and (b) BUDGET_MS 680 — neither caused nor fixed the 504s (they ran 5.5h AFTER the BUDGET_MS deploy and stopped exactly when geo WRITES stopped, 3.5h BEFORE the Supabase resize). Read the REAL error bytes (e.errors[0]) before blaming infra; correlate the symptom's start/stop against the actual workload, not against whatever was deployed.
63 A backfill lap that throws OR fails to advance but lets the cron fire return HTTP 200 is a SILENT failure — geo was DEAD 4h under green 200s with the error masked as "[object Object]". Every drain fire must return ok:false/failed:N + console.error for ANY thrown/non-200 lap (ALL platforms); a dead/non-advancing lap can never read as a green fire. (LORAMER_GOOGLE_QUOTA_GUARD_V1 CHANGE 1.)
64 TWO completion authorities that can disagree are a stall trap: the sync_state cursor backfill_complete (writer) vs platform_connections.onboard_steps_done (drain). A stale done-flag over an INCOMPLETE cursor silently SKIPS a client forever (Woo Shelley: onboard ['woo'] done but cursor complete=false at 2018-12-13, owes to ~2015 — frozen ~12d; drain pending filter excludes her). The cursor must be the SINGLE completion authority; any path that re-opens a cursor to complete=false MUST clear that step key from onboard_steps_done.
65 Woo backfill "complete = one 21-day all-status-ZERO chunk" (woocommerce-backfill.ts) can FALSE-complete on any >21-day sales GAP mid-history — a quiet store stretch reads as history-start. When hardening woo completeness: probe the store's true oldest order, or require N consecutive zero chunks.
66 supabase-js .upsert(row) WITHOUT an explicit { onConflict } defaults its conflict target to the PRIMARY KEY. On a table whose real dedup key is a SECONDARY UNIQUE column (meta_tokens: PK=id + UNIQUE(user_email)), and where the PK is auto-generated (no id in the row), the upsert becomes an INSERT → it violates the secondary UNIQUE → 409, and if the returned error is discarded the write is a SILENT no-op that still looks successful. This bit the Meta callback: re-auth never rewrote the token (only the first-ever connect worked; the success redirect fired regardless), which broke the cote@ refresh. RULE: every upsert names its conflict target explicitly ({ onConflict: '<the-unique-column>' }) AND checks the returned error (fail loud — redirect/throw, never swallow, per L15). Gate-A a token/dedup upsert by reproducing the SECOND write to an existing key: buggy path 409s, fixed path UPDATES in place (id stable, 1 row). (LORAMER_META_CALLBACK_ONCONFLICT_V1, 2026-07-02.)
67 A Gate-A that checks only STATUS CODES can pass while the BEHAVIOR is broken — assert the behavior the gate exists to protect, not just 2xx/3xx. Origin: the 138a820 legacy-surface middleware silently broke the signup funnel two ways and that flight's Gate-A missed BOTH because it only read status codes: (a) it gated /agency + /business — the PRE-AUTH two-door signup pages — so unauthenticated new users were bounced to /login (the pages' content was never read → public marketing doors misclassified as "legacy tenant pages"); (b) it redirected /dashboard → -next BEFORE the /dashboard layout's enforceWelcomeGate could fire, so a fresh user reached the empty -next portfolio with NO account_type (Add-client 409s). The Gate-A even OBSERVED break (b) — /dashboard-next/clients returned 200 for a brand-new no-account_type user — and read it as "not over-blocked" instead of "onboarding didn't fire." RULE: for any gate/redirect/auth change, (1) READ what each matched path actually IS before gating it (public vs authed, data vs marketing), and (2) assert the POSITIVE behavior it must preserve — "a fresh user is REDIRECTED to /welcome", "the door RENDERS unauthenticated" — a bare 200 or 307 is necessary, NEVER sufficient. (LORAMER_SIGNUP_FUNNEL_FIX_V1, 2026-07-14.)
(2026-06-22) Product/line grain must reconcile to its account grain on the SAME revenue basis; re-capture history ONLY AFTER the basis fix ships (re-capturing before forces a second pass — violates "never twice").
